Funeral Bells Ring, Airplanes Soar Over Southern Country for King's Funeral 45

Procession Two Miles Long, Solemn and Respectful

Dignitaries from Various Countries Bear the Coffin, Utmost Honor

Belgrade: Today at noon, the funeral of the Southern King was held at the local cathedral. The ceremony was simple but extremely solemn. The surroundings in the hall were all draped in black. The participants were extremely quiet, and only the sound of bells, cannons, the roar of airplanes in the sky, and the clear chanting of scriptures in the hall could be heard. Members of the royal family knelt beside the coffin, and Romanian King Carol stood in front of the coffin with a sword. A high-ranking bishop solemnly praised the achievements of the Southern King. After the ceremony, the coffin was placed on a gun carriage. The young new king, accompanied by his mother and grandmother, as well as the King of Romania, the English Prince, the French President, the Polish Prime Minister, and General Göring, followed the gun carriage in an orderly fashion. They passed through the thoroughfare for about two miles. Tens of thousands of spectators lined the streets, and the military police provided extremely careful protection, directly to the station. The coffin was then moved onto the train, ready to be transported to Topola to be buried in the royal mausoleum. Airplanes from France, Czechoslovakia, and Romania soared in the sky, paying their final respects to the unfortunate Southern King who was killed. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Church Ceremony Complete, Coffin Departs 46

Capital of Yugoslavia: The funeral of former King Alexander I was held this morning. At 8:15 a.m., Bishop Bernabé held a memorial service at the cathedral. Young King Peter II, members of the royal family, French President Lebrun, Romanian King Carol, the Southern Regent, diplomatic representatives from various countries, and delegations from various cities in the Southern country all participated in the prayer. The bishop gave a speech, mourning the former king and wishing the ideals of Yugoslavian unity would last forever. At this point, the coffin began to depart. The military fired cannons. More than a hundred airplanes from Yugoslavia, France, Czechoslovakia, and Romania soared in the sky. Funeral bells rang in all the churches throughout the city. At the front of the procession were troops from Yugoslavia and various foreign countries, followed by disabled veterans of the previous war, then nineteen carts of fresh flowers, followed by the coffin. Behind the coffin were Queen Mother Marie, the new King Peter II, heads of state and royalty from various countries. When the procession began to advance, many of the people on the roadside sobbed and wept, and some cried out loud. When they saw the young king, they all cheered. At 11 a.m., the coffin arrived at the train station. The troops lined up and saluted the coffin. Then the coffin was carried onto a special train. The royal family and dignitaries also boarded the train. The special train departed for Topola at 11:25 a.m. and was buried in the Karađorđević royal mausoleum in the basement of the city's church. (18th Havas Telegram)

Strict Security Along the Route 47

Belgrade: This afternoon, the funeral of the late King Alexander was held. Many members of the royal family and dignitaries from various countries came here to bear the coffin. The distance from the cathedral to the station will be a two-mile walk. The police authorities have taken strict precautions. Troops are lined up shoulder to shoulder along the route to prevent anyone from blocking the road. Only students are allowed to stand on one side of the road, so the police can focus their full attention on the other side where the public is allowed to stand. All windows along the route must be closed. The public is not allowed to scatter flowers or carry any objects, even umbrellas are prohibited. All side streets will be cleared, and no one is allowed to walk in them. Spectators must stand in their positions by 7 a.m., and they can only move when the king's coffin has boarded the train and left for Topola. Thousands of detectives will be mixed in with the spectators to prevent any traitors.

The preliminary trial judge also summoned Lai Qiqu for questioning. According to his confession, he was born in 1903 in the Croatian region of Yugoslavia and worked as a farmer. He recently resided in the Croatian refugee camp in Yangkashishti, Hungary. Regarding the situation and mission of this trip to France, Lai Qiqu's claims are the same as those of Bospisić, with only slight differences in the details. In fact, the various police affairs sections of the Police Affairs Bureau manage the personnel of the police, so no military police are used. When the official system is established, it is planned to explain it in detail. The configuration of personnel and the attitude of the military police commander, etc., once clearly determined, will naturally eliminate the fear of military police. In short, from the spirit of the dual system, if the military police, consulates, and Kwantung Agency police are separated and independent, each governing its own way, as is currently the case, the implementation of the national policy towards Manchuria is particularly inappropriate. Considering Kwantung Prefecture and its affiliated territories, its importance will increase in the future, and the result of the command system is deeply felt. Therefore, the original plan is adhered to. The army not only has no intention of dictatorship, but also hopes to proceed with civilian administration. According to the current situation, it is necessary for the development of Manchuria to have only this degree of military action, which is inevitable. I deeply believe that the function of the police organs in Manchuria can be fully exerted by this. Although it is impossible to know how the situation in the field will change, the attitude of the military police in the field will be more cautious in the future. Governor Lingari also pays attention to this point. Due to budget relations, the official system will be promulgated after the temporary parliament. The outline of the official system will be announced first. (18th Communication Telegram)

Chairman Shen Baozhang resolved the following matters: (1) On the issue of uniform vehicle tax collection, it was resolved that foreign vehicles would be the standard for tax collection, with passenger and freight vehicles divided into three classes. (3) On the issue of Fujian Province joining the committee because roads have been built in northern Fujian that can connect to Jiangxi and Zhejiang, it was unanimously welcomed. (4) On the issue of amending the regulations, it was resolved that it was approved. The meeting adjourned at around 5:00 PM. Unresolved cases will be discussed tomorrow. (18th Dispatch)

Northwest Inspection Notes by Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

Recent Situation of Civil Affairs in Gansu Province 96

Since the revolution, Gansu has been a place where warlords have been entrenched, levying exorbitant taxes to meet the needs of internal warfare. Coupled with various water and drought disasters and chaotic currency, the rural economy has been in a slump. The people live in dire straits and suffer unspeakable hardship. As for local administrative affairs such as education and construction, in the warlord era, there was only destruction and no construction. The disturbances of Ma Tingxian and Lei Zhongtian, and the ravages of the Northwest Army, caused the people of the whole province to bear tens of millions of yuan in paper money alone. In addition, they had to bear more than 800,000 yuan for military meals every month, and the army levied grain and fodder locally, shortening the lives of more than six million people in the province. Even as recently as the period when Shao Lizi was chairman of the provincial government in the 21st year (of the Republic), local soldiers surrounded the provincial government and forcibly demanded military expenses. In the 22nd year, the provincial government was reorganized, and the central government sent Zhu to take over as chairman of the provincial government and concurrent Pacification Commissioner of Gansu, Ningxia, and Qinghai provinces, and dispatched the entire First Division to defend the southern border of Gansu. Thus, the Gansu situation, which required reform in all aspects, began to gradually get on the right track. The recent situation of civil affairs will be briefly described below.

The police administration in this province has been largely unsuccessful in the past. Recently, the Civil Affairs Department, in view of the province's years of disasters and the ravaged state of the local areas, has formulated temporary measures for reducing and retaining public security bureaus in various counties to reduce the burden on the people. Public security bureaus with an annual public security budget of less than 5,000 yuan, or with no budget and relying on temporary levies from the people, will be temporarily abolished and merged into the county government. The public security bureaus to be abolished include 26 counties, including Gangu and Liangdang in Longnan, Heshui and Zhuanglang in Longdong, and Yumen and Dunhuang in Longxi. The remaining 11 counties, such as Wudu, Chengxian, Wenxian, and Kangxian, are close to bandit areas, and their public security bureaus have been reorganized into standing teams of county defense regiments to reduce the burden on the people. As for the director training center for long-term police attached to the provincial public security bureau, because it is an academic institution, it is allowed to extend its time to train police talent.

The establishment of defense regiments in this province also began this year. In the past, the people of various counties, although they provided their own guns and weapons to defend their local areas, lacked training and organization. If the leadership was not appropriate, they often went astray and became a scourge to the local areas. For the sake of local pacification, the Civil Affairs Department first established standing teams of defense regiments in 11 counties, including Wenxian, to create a public force to prepare the villages for self-defense and to prevent bandits from using their cunning skills. The method is for the county magistrate to concurrently serve as the captain of the standing army, with an additional deputy captain to assist. Since the establishment of standing teams in various counties, banditry has gradually subsided and order has been stabilized.

As for self-government, there is little to commend in local self-government in this province. However, recently, each district chief has reorganized the autonomous organizations below the district level with graduates of the training institute for autonomous personnel, and household registration surveys have been carried out in each county in order. However, the autonomous funds in each county are uneven, and the work cannot be carried out uniformly. Regarding the survey items, each county has few detailed and clear reports. In fact, the district and township chiefs are only collectors of money for the county government (or tax collectors). Therefore, it is like climbing a tree to catch a fish to expect the autonomous organs below the district level to be the engine of local public undertakings such as education and hygiene. To promote self-government, it is necessary to first train the people and cultivate their ability to govern themselves. Otherwise, there will only be autonomous organs without autonomous functions, or even let the organs be controlled by local bullies to oppress the people. The people's suffering will deepen, and self-government will be counterproductive. This province is located in a remote border area, with a complex mix of ethnic groups. More than 90% of the villagers are illiterate, and years of disasters have impoverished the local areas to the extreme. Autonomous organs are inherently positive construction, but the public's awareness is weak and their knowledge is backward. They think that the autonomous organs are descendants of the county government, established solely for the purpose of collecting taxes and food, and do not know how to urge themselves to improve. The success of local self-government is still far off.

As for hygiene, this province initially had no hygiene facilities. In addition to the provincial and municipal aspects, where the provincial public security bureau is responsible for the city's hygiene, the county public security bureaus are responsible for the hygiene in various counties. However, the public security bureaus do not have specialized hygiene personnel or hygiene equipment and medicines. Usually, the hygiene work they do is largely limited to cleaning streets and transporting garbage. Although there are clinics attached to the clinics in the summer, they are not necessarily perfect due to limited funds and personnel. Even the review of the qualifications of doctors and the inspection of the sale of medicines in the city are not properly handled. Fortunately, recently, the central government has paid attention to the hygiene undertakings in the northwestern provinces and has established an epidemic prevention office in Lanzhou. According to the person in charge of preparations, the office is divided into two departments: the human medical department and the veterinary department. Each department has several groups, and each group has a director in charge of all the undertakings of the group. The office is currently under construction and will be completed in about five months. Recently, the provincial government has also established the Gansu Provincial Hygiene Inspection Office to work with the epidemic prevention office to handle the province's hygiene undertakings. Animal diseases, seasonal epidemics, and infectious diseases, which have always been considered incurable, will be fundamentally addressed.

As for relief, this province has suffered many major disasters in recent years, and the number of people who have fled is unknown. Therefore, relief undertakings are urgently needed. In addition to issuing orders to various county governments to urge them to follow the regulations on the management of local granaries issued internally, the Civil Affairs Department has also requested the provincial government to approve the allocation of regular funds to establish relief institutions such as relief homes and loan offices in the provincial capital, and to remit tax silver and field grain for disaster victims. Recently, county governments that have violated orders to collect remitted silver and grain from disaster victims have also been investigated and punished by the provincial government.

The quality of officialdom depends on whether or not the right people are appointed. There are those in charge of county administration who can be honest and determined to be good officials, but it is a pity that they are few and far between. As for others, such as those with old and corrupt ideas, or those who are just filling positions and drawing salaries, they are too busy to flatter their superiors, so how can they have time to pay attention to reform and important matters? This situation is almost a common problem in various places. Today, if we want the officialdom to get on track as soon as possible, we must severely urge them on.

Recent News on the Sichuan Army's Bandit Suppression 97

Defense of Jialing River Area Consolidated

He and Xiao's Bandit Units Suffer Losses in Guizhou

According to a communication from Hankou, Liu Xiang, Commander-in-Chief of the Sichuan Bandit Suppression, has repeatedly received telegrams from Chairman Chiang urging him to resume his post and continue to be responsible for bandit suppression. Although there seem to be concerns about the resumption of his post, he has not hesitated to direct military affairs. At the beginning of this month, the various armies, under Liu's command, launched an offensive against the bandits and have made considerable progress. The morale of the troops is very high, and the defense of the Jialing River area is particularly consolidated. Arrangements for the deployment of troops, the relief and emergency aid to refugees, and the promotion of political work are being earnestly planned.

He Long and Xiao Ke's two bandit units originally intended to enter Sichuan at the same time, but they suffered heavy losses due to the suppression by the troops stationed in various provinces, and their goal was ultimately difficult to achieve. He's bandit unit was forced into Guizhou from Ganlongkou in Sichuan, fleeing through Huoshaochang, Xiyangba, Pingdongkou, and Hongshiban. They are now trapped in Yutan. Xiao's bandit unit was surrounded and attacked by the joint forces of Sichuan, Guizhou, and Guangxi, and has been hiding in the mountains. They have repeatedly tried to cross the Zhenyuan River without success and are likely to be wiped out first. The Sichuan Bandit Suppression Headquarters telegraphed Hankou on the 17th to announce the victory, saying, "Xiao's bandit unit fled to Guizhou and, after being encircled and attacked by various armies, has been hiding in the deep mountains in the vicinity of Shiqian, Shibing, and Yuqing. He's bandit unit moved from the border of Sichuan and Hubei to the border of Guizhou and was attacked by a certain division of a certain regiment from Shazichang, and was defeated. The bandits retreated towards Yutan on the 14th, and are currently being pursued and suppressed." (17th)

Completion of the Qingdao Dockyard 98

Grand Scale and Novel Machinery

Qingdao Correspondence: Jiaozhou is the only good harbor in North China, with a depth exceeding thirty to forty feet and impervious to severe cold. During the German administration, Longma Road was established as a marketplace, and wharves were built, along with the Jiaoji Railway, facilitating convenient land and sea transportation. Commerce flourished, and the once desolate fishing village transformed into a renowned port in the Orient. Subsequently, as the number of ships entering and leaving the port increased daily, a floating dock was specially constructed for repairs, providing convenience to shipping merchants. In the early years of the Republic, with the outbreak of the European War, the Japanese replaced the Germans. Given the proximity of Jiaozhou to Dalian (Lüda), large ships could be conveniently repaired at the Dalian dockyard. Additionally, two small slipways with a capacity of only a few hundred tons were built in the harbor for repairing smaller vessels, while the original floating dock was shipped back to Germany. After Qingdao's recovery, despite the municipal government's utmost efforts, little attention was paid to port affairs for a decade. However, after the appointment of Shen Honglie as the Commander of the Northeast Navy and Mayor of Qingdao, the port of Jiaozhou became the lifeline of Qingdao.

Page 8

Numerous Chinese and foreign shipping companies operated transport ships, and the number of ships entering and leaving the port reached thousands. Looking across North China, only the Dagukou dockyard was capable of ship repairs, but its scale was small, its equipment simple, and the siltation of the Baihe River was severe. Ships with a draft exceeding ten feet could not enter for repairs, a natural deficiency. As for the Jiangnan shipyards, the distance was too far. Small steamers navigating between Qingdao, Weihai, Qingdao, Yantai, and Qingdao, Haizhou, suffered from the long and perilous voyages and dared not venture there lightly. Even if they did, they incurred both time and economic losses, forcing them to suspend operations, greatly affecting Qingdao. To promote the prosperity of Qingdao and for the convenience of shipping merchants, Shen Honglie raised substantial funds to construct a grand dockyard. In the 21st year of the Republic, the site was selected at Taiping Bay in Xiaogang, and construction commenced, completed in September of this year. The Shanghai Fook Kee Construction Company was the contractor, while the Naval Factory was commissioned to oversee the construction. The dockyard is scheduled to hold its completion ceremony on the 20th of this month. Details of the dockyard are recorded as follows:

The bottom and surrounding walls of the dock are entirely hewn from hydraulic rock, with the surface paved with Laoshan granite. The solidity of the foundation and the magnificence of the surface surpass all other dockyards in the country.

The construction of the dockyard, its size and width, must be proportionate. If it is too wide, timber is wasted; if it is too narrow, sunlight cannot easily penetrate, making work inconvenient and paint difficult to dry quickly. The design of the dockyard is based on the latest scientific theories, with suitable size and well-proportioned parts. The width of the dock bottom is fifty feet, gradually widening from the third stone of the dock wall, each level increasing by one foot in height and width, fitting the curved part of the ship's hull. At the eleventh level, the width is thirty inches, facilitating work. From the twelfth layer of stone, every forty-seven inches in height, it extends outward by one foot, totaling five sections and expanding outward by five feet, forming a vertical line to support the ship's sides. The dock gate has two sections: the first extends to the dock head and is four hundred and eighty feet long, and the second extends to the dock head and is three hundred and fifty-six feet long. The water depth above the wooden blocks is thirteen feet. For larger ships, the gate can be moved to the first section; for smaller ships, the gate can be moved to the second section. The water volume is reduced, and expenses are naturally reduced accordingly. On the left, right, and front ends of the dockyard, there are six convenient paths. From the third layer of the stone wall at the bottom, there are thirty-seven steps, each with a height of 1.5 feet and a width ranging from 5 to 7 feet, sloping at about fifty degrees. Multiple workers can ascend and descend simultaneously without feeling crowded, offering convenience and safety comparable to the staircase of a large hotel. At the ends of the dock, there are two slipways equipped with pulleys and winches for transporting materials, proving quite convenient. The center of the dock bottom is slightly higher, sloping to the left and right, with a clear water ditch around the perimeter. Accumulated water drains into the ditch and then flows into the pumping pit, keeping the dock bottom clean and dry. Within the two gates, there are rudder pits for removing and repairing ship rudders. The central wooden keel block on the dock bottom is made of reinforced concrete, with a beam running from the dock head to the dock tail, uniting hundreds of blocks into one, providing greater safety and durability compared to the old-style cast iron blocks. There are also eleven sliding keel blocks on the left and right, laid on iron rails, and four sliding wheel platforms are installed from the dock bottom to the dock surface. When the ship's keel is about to land on the keel blocks, manpower is only needed on the dock surface to move the ropes to the left and right, allowing the sliding wheels to closely adhere to the bottom of the ship, eliminating the need for additional personnel to go underwater to place the keel blocks, a distinctive feature.

In the past, old-fashioned water pumps were all volute type, like the paddle wheels of Yangtze River steamers, with less efficiency. This dockyard uses the latest propeller-type water pumps from the British Vickers factory, similar to the screw propellers of modern ships. The novelty of the design and the magnitude of the effectiveness are unprecedented in Chinese dockyards. There are two machines, each with a 24-inch inlet and a 30-inch outlet, capable of pumping 50,000 gallons of water per minute, approximately 82 tons. The water inside the dock can be drained within three hours, illustrating its great capacity. Each motor is connected to the water pump, rotating at 977 revolutions per minute, with 200 horsepower each. Additionally, there is a separate 7-inch small water pump for temporary drainage of leaks. These machines are all installed in reinforced concrete rooms below ground, occupying very little space and being very easy to manage, another distinctive feature.

Relief-Through-Work Plan in Anhui Province 99

Total Funding Required: Four Million Yuan

Anqing Correspondence: This year, Anhui Province suffered from a severe drought, affecting a vast area. The Anhui Provincial Government drafted a disaster relief plan, ready for implementation. However, due to the Provincial Treasury's financial constraints, it was difficult to implement. Therefore, the scope of the disaster relief work was carefully revised into a relief-through-work plan, submitted to the headquarters of the three provinces' bandit suppression for review and approval. The main points of the plan are as follows: (A) Dredging of Important Rivers. 1. The Wan River and Ji River: Implement relief-through-work dredging of the lower reaches, including (1) the main line of the Wan River, from Yanhekou in the west of Tongcheng, upstream through Jiu Bin Port, Shiku, Shipai, Laoya Tan, Shi Gongdu, Youqi Pu, to Yingjiang Port; (2) the tributary line of the Qian River, from Laoya Tan upstream through Hejia Zha, Xiongjia Bu, and Wangjia He. The total length of the two lines is 195 kilometers. Before detailed on-site measurements and determination of cross-sectional designs, the scope is temporarily set at an average of 12,000 cubic meters of earth excavated per kilometer, totaling 2.34 million cubic meters. Assuming each worker can excavate 0.2 cubic meters per day, this can accommodate 11.7 million workdays, or 13,000 disaster-stricken people for three months. The relief is set at 10 cents per cubic meter, requiring 234,000 yuan. Surveying and engineering management fees will be listed separately. 2. The Zongyang River, Guache River, Dong River, and Chang River: Implement relief-through-work dredging, including (1) the Zongyang River, from the Jiangkou of Zongyang Town upstream through Changhe and Shouyi Lake; (2) the Guache River, from the Yazi Lakekou in the western part of Caizi Lake upstream through Tanglin, Meizhu Ta, and Xin'an Ferry to Lao Meishu Street; (3) the Dong River, from the Tuqiao Huihekou upstream, connecting Shanxi Lake, Chenyang Lake, Baitang Lake, and Zhu Da Lake; (4) the Yan Chang River, from the end of the Zhu Da River upstream through Yangjia Zui, Yan Jia Du, to Jiehekou. The total length is 150 kilometers. Following the Wan River method, it requires excavating 1.8 million cubic meters of earth, accommodating 8,000 disaster-stricken people for three months, requiring 180,000 yuan calculated using the Wan River method. 3. The Yu River: Dredge from the Yu River Estuary upstream through Weijia Town, Tucao Town, Huanglihe Town, Chaoxian County, to the eastern part of Chaohu Lake at Hugangkou. The construction length is 110 kilometers, requiring excavating 1.32 million cubic meters of earth, accommodating over 7,300 disaster-stricken people for three months, requiring 122,000 yuan. 4. The Shishou Waterway in Chaohu Lake: Dredge from Zhongmiao through Shishou to the Hefei County seat, approximately 55 kilometers long. (1) The 20-kilometer section from Zhongmiao to Shishou will be dredged to a depth of 1.5 meters, with a bottom width of 10 meters and a slope of 1:2, requiring approximately 160,000 cubic meters of earth, to be dredged by a dredging machine. (2) The 35-kilometer section from Shishou to Hefei County will be dredged to an average depth of 1.5 meters, with the bottom width narrowed as appropriate, requiring approximately 300,000 cubic meters of earth. Disaster-stricken labor will assist in the first section, while the second section will entirely rely on disaster-stricken labor. Together, this can employ 3,000 disaster-stricken people for more than three months, requiring a total of 142,000 yuan. 5. The Qingyi River, Shuiyang River, and Luming River: (1) The main line of the Qingyi River, from the Wuhu Estuary, through Changhe Xiang, Pujiadian, Qing Shuihe, turning south through Tiancheng Yi and Tai Liangwei and Fangcun Town, Wanzhi Town, to Xihe Town; (2) the first tributary line of the Qingyi River, from Dong Liangshan Jiajiang, through Da Danghe, Jingzhuangmen, connecting to Biandan River to Pujiadian, and east to the main line; (3) the second tributary line of the Qingyi River, taking Yang Qinghe from Qing Shuihe, connecting Erli Geng, and communicating with Shuiyang; (4) the main line of the Shuiyang River, from the Dangtu Jinzhuguan Outer Estuary, along the Gu Xihe River, through Hejiawan, Sanli Tang, Huangchi, Wuxi, Yanchi, to Shuiyang Town; (5) the main line of the Luming River, from the Lugang Estuary, through Yiqiao, Shipao, to Huang Mu Ferry. The above five lines are planned for dredging a total of 330 kilometers, requiring 2.76 million cubic meters of earth to be excavated, accommodating 15,500 disaster-stricken people for four months, requiring 276,000 yuan. 6. The Tanhe River Source: It is proposed that the Huai River Leading Committee and the Anhui Province share the cost, budgeting 300,000 yuan. The above-mentioned dredging portion of item A, totaling approximately 950 kilometers in length, requires an estimated expenditure of 1,264,000 yuan, plus surveying and engineering management fees, estimated at 5% or approximately 66,000 yuan, for a total of 1,330,000 yuan. (B) Dredging of ditches, canals, ponds, and embankments: listed at 520,000 yuan. (C) Repairing of dangerous sections of dikes, culverts, and sluice gates on the Yangtze River, Huai River, lakes, and rivers: temporarily listed at 600,000 yuan. (D) Constructing roads in disaster areas: approximately 650 kilometers are planned, requiring 650,000 yuan. (E) Enhancing disaster prevention equipment: (1) Establishing a Xushui pumping station, requiring approximately 100,000 yuan; (2) Surveying water storage areas, including surveying and hydrological measurements, costing approximately 150,000 yuan; (3) Implementing two major water conservancy development projects: (1) Implementing the Huayang River water-saving project, planned in three phases, requiring a total expenditure of 2,033,000 yuan, with the first phase needing immediate implementation, costing 500,000 yuan; (2) Implementing the Yinli project, requiring 150,000 yuan. The total funding required for the above six items (A, B, C, D, E, and F) is 4,000,000 yuan. (16th)

Salt Workers from Twelve Forts Petition the Jiangsu Provincial Government 100

Demanding the Preservation of Combined Sailing and Steam Transport and the Abolition of the "Miao Envoy" Measures

Zhenjiang News: Since last year, when the "Miao Envoy" (referring to a salt transport commissioner surnamed Miao) reformed the salt transport system, abolishing sailing transport and switching entirely to steam transport, the livelihoods of over 200,000 salt workers from the Twelve Forts area were threatened with collapse. At that time, salt workers from the area sent representatives to petition the Ministry of Finance and the Jiangsu Provincial Government, demanding the preservation of combined sailing and steam transport. After repeated discussions between Minister Kong and the Jiangsu Provincial Government representative Wang Boling, a compromise was agreed upon, and an agreement was made on how to negotiate a settlement. The salt worker unrest was then calmed. Recently, however, the "Miao Envoy" Qiu Jie, stubbornly insisted on steam transport and drafted three settlement measures: "Hemp Bag Factory," "Immigration for Employment," and "Subsidized Vessel Conversion," submitting them to the ministry for record. Recently, he has been actively implementing these measures, sending a certain Ma to Twelve Forts to purchase salt vessels for factory conversion and ordering the Seven Companies to relocate north. The salt workers have become greatly alarmed and have once again sent over 4,000 representatives to the provincial capital to petition. The details are as follows:

Arrival in the Provincial Capital: The total number of boat owners and salt workers in the Twelve Forts area is no less than ten thousand. After holding meetings, each boat sent two representatives, and the transport workers also sent some representatives, totaling over 4,000 people, led by the chief representatives Yang Huaisheng, Yang Desheng, Wang Mingyi, Xu Jinyuan, and Zhu Zhaoluan. At dawn on the 17th, they chartered three tugboats, towing dozens of civilian boats, carrying over a thousand petitioners from the fort to Zhenjiang. They arrived at around 10 a.m., disembarked, and headed to the provincial government to petition. In the afternoon, a second group of over 700 people arrived, with the entire crowd gathered on the road to the provincial government, causing congestion.

The Petitioning Process: After the salt workers arrived at their destination, the five representatives, including Zhu Zhaoluan, presented their cards to request a meeting with Chairman Chen. As Chen was in Beijing on official business, the section chief, Wan Junmo, met with them in his place. The representatives stated that the "Miao Envoy" had overturned the combined sailing and steam transport measures, ordered the Seven Companies to relocate north, and drafted measures to establish factories, relocate for employment, and subsidize vessel conversion, destroying the means of livelihood that the salt workers had depended on for generations and cutting off their means of survival. They requested that the central ministries be informed and that the salt workers' demands be accommodated: (1) abolish the three measures of the "Miao Envoy" and withdraw their record filing; (2) preserve sailing transport; (3) revoke the order for the Seven Companies to relocate north. Wan promised to forward the request to Chairman Chen upon his return to Zhenjiang and also promised to telegraph Wang Weiyuan to come to Zhenjiang to discuss solutions, and he advised the representatives to return first to avoid trouble.

Sleeping in the Open: The representatives, feeling that their demands had not been fully resolved, decided to gather and wait outside the provincial government until Chairman Chen returned to Zhenjiang to resolve the issue. As night fell, most of them brought rice straw mats and bedding, huddling together in the cold wind, their situation extremely miserable. However, their firm determination was not diminished by this suffering. It is said that there are still over a thousand people who, because the ships were loaded yesterday, are scheduled to come to Zhenjiang today to join the petition.

Military and Police Maintaining Order: After receiving news of the salt workers' petition in Zhenjiang, the provincial capital's Public Security Bureau dispatched a large number of police officers to monitor the scene, prohibiting smoking and lighting fires to prevent fires. The Special Operations Battalion of the Security Department also sent troops armed with rifles to maintain order. Fortunately, the petitioning salt workers were able to obey the command and maintain order, so there was no opportunity for troublemakers to take advantage of the situation. According to the representatives, if they do not receive a satisfactory response from the provincial government, they plan to go to Beijing to petition Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance. (18th)

Sun Lanqin of Songjiang Dies Suddenly in the Fields 101

Sun Lanqin, a villager from He Ying in the 14th district of Fengjing, was in his fifties. His wife, surnamed Ma, was of a similar age. They were tenants at Fei's residence in Zhenxi. Lanqin and his son, Songpo, cultivated the land at home, and the family lived harmoniously. On the 16th of this month, the father and son were at home. The next day, at around 10 a.m., his nephew, Langan, was passing through the fields when he saw his uncle Lanqin lying dead in the fields, covered in blood. Realizing that something had happened, he ran to inform his aunt, Ma. Upon returning to the village and seeing the scene, Ma was extremely grieved and immediately reported it to the Second Branch Bureau, which forwarded it to the County Public Security Bureau to request the court to conduct an autopsy. The cause of Sun Lanqin's death is unknown. However, since Lanqin's death, his son, Songpo, has suddenly disappeared, leading local people to speculate.

Re-Appointment of Township Chiefs in the First District 102

Following the county magistrate's decision to merge townships in the first district of this county, it was imperative to re-select township chiefs and deputies. After being selected, a list was submitted to the county magistrate for approval to facilitate the handling of baojia (local security system) matters. The district chief, Li Yi, followed orders to compile a register of candidates for township chiefs and deputies for the 20th year of the Republic. The county has now approved the list and issued instructions, informing the selected township chiefs and deputies and reporting the date of their appointment for approval. Among the town chiefs in this district, only the Longtan Town chief was replaced by Huang Han, while the rest were re-appointed to their original positions.

New Developments in the Suzhou Land Tax Fraud Case 103

The land tax fraud case in Wuxian, which has caused a sensation in society, has been under investigation by two commissioners, Dong and Fang, dispatched by the Ministry of Finance to Suzhou. Initially, they uncovered fraudulent activities in the private collection of taxes, arresting the register manager, Qian Zhonghua, and detaining him at the County Security Team headquarters to await further action. Subsequently, after a detailed investigation into the hidden wasteland section for a month, they discovered that old, long-term wasteland registers had been falsified by underreporting the amount of taxable land. On the night of the 17th, Commissioner Dong, together with Section Chief Dong of the county government, searched the residence of the land tax collection director, Zhu Xijun. After consulting with the Wuxian county magistrate, the county magistrate ordered the removal of Zhu Xijun from his position as director of the land tax collection office, pending investigation, and appointed the deputy director, Gu Xiangji, as the new director, and appointed a Lin to be the new deputy director. Zhu Xijun was summoned to the county government and temporarily placed under surveillance, awaiting provincial orders. Commissioner Dong took a train to the province yesterday (the 18th) to seek instructions. It is reported that the old register, Wu Taijing, and the register room managers, clerks, and surveyors of the five districts are all suspected of colluding in the fraud. The Wuxian county magistrate summoned all the staff of the land tax collection office yesterday morning (the 18th) and stated that the responsibility for the land tax fraud case rests solely with Director Zhu and will not involve others, so all staff can continue to work in peace. The new director, Gu Xiangqing, took office yesterday (the 18th) and is in the process of taking over. Whether the case will be transferred to the province or to the court for handling remains to be determined by provincial orders. However, the contents of the case are very complex and are unlikely to be resolved within a few days.

Villagers in Nanhui Destroy the Fire Prevention Association 104

Gentry, merchants, and villagers of Sandun Town in Nanhui County raised funds to build a Fire Prevention Association in the Yangshe Temple in the town's Chayang community to prevent disasters. The association was established on National Day. On the 13th, villagers Pan Gentang, Pan Molin, and others gathered several hundred people to the town, falsely claiming that the Fire Prevention Association had encroached on the site of the Yangshe Temple and had to be destroyed. The town chief reported the matter to the district office. The district chief, Zhang Bangjie, went to the town to mediate, but to no avail. The walls and roof of the Fire Prevention Association's premises were destroyed, and the crowd dispersed.

Butchers in Wuxi Resume Business Yesterday 105

The fresh meat business in the urban area of this county has been in dispute with the slaughter tax office over tax collection. Four meat shop workers were detained, leading to a strike by the entire industry and petitions to party and government authorities, as reported yesterday. It is now learned that the industry, after being persuaded by County Magistrate Yan and the County Chamber of Commerce to resume business, is quietly waiting for a resolution. The detained shop workers, Li Bingsheng and Guo Zhiyuan, and two others, were released by County Magistrate Yan after ordering the Public Security Bureau to transfer them to the County Government for interrogation. The County Chamber of Commerce convened a meeting of meat industry representatives Sui Zongyi, Wei Shuzhou, Ren Shuji, Wang Zhongxian, Li Chengde, and others at 10 a.m. yesterday (the 18th). Chamber of Commerce Chairman Yang Hanxi, Chen Zhanru, Cheng Jingtang, and others successively persuaded the representatives. However, the discussion on spot tax collection ended without any benefit to the meat merchants. They insisted on mediation according to the previous agreement to increase the tax by five yuan, but the tax office claimed that the spot tax collection had resulted in losses of approximately 2,000 yuan, which should be compensated by the meat merchants. The meat merchants refused, and the mediation ended without any result.

Party and Government Meeting in Jiangyin Plans to Open Huangtiangang Port 106

The Zhenjiang Branch of the Customs Office, after being requested by the County Chamber of Commerce and others and approved by the Revenue Department, has been changed to a loading and unloading port for scheduled ships. Local figures such as Ji Xiangxiang, to promote the local economy, planned to build lighters and warehouses. However, due to limited local financial resources, they contacted the Shanghai Commercial Bank for investment and visited various ports along the Yangtze River for investigation. The Shanghai Bank is currently planning the investment. However, the key point of whether or not to invest is whether Huangtiangang Port will be dredged this winter, which is a major issue. The party and government held a meeting at the county government on the 16th to discuss the development plan and submitted it to the provincial department for review and approval of subsidies so that construction could begin as soon as possible.

Burglaries Occur Frequently in the Four Townships of Changzhou 107

This year, Wuyi suffered from a severe drought, and before the winter season arrived, burglaries have already occurred frequently in the four townships. At around 1 a.m. on the 17th, a group of armed bandits suddenly came to the home of Yang Xianquan in Zhongyin Township, in the first district. While they were firing shots to intimidate, a security guard who was patrolling nearby heard the gunshots and immediately went forward to apprehend them. He captured one bandit, Chen Suo'er. He was then transferred to the first substation of the Public Security Bureau in the West Gate. After being questioned by the patrol officer, Tang Renjie, he learned the whereabouts of his accomplices and immediately dispatched police to the city wall of the South Gate, capturing two bandits, Shao Jiannan and Qiu Xiaojing. He then captured two suspects, Shi Hebao and Zhang Guiqing, under the East Gate water gate. After repeated questioning, they were transferred to the Public Security Bureau for questioning. On the previous day, the home of Zhou A'gen in Gouzhuang Township in the sixth district was also robbed. Dozens of bandits came and searched the house at will, taking away all of his 1,630 yuan in silver dollars and all of his clothes. The loss was extremely great. Under such circumstances, the villagers are unable to sleep peacefully at night.

The Yangzhou Huai Salt Relocation Crisis Subsides 108

Various circles in Yangzhou have repeatedly appealed to the relevant authorities regarding the Jinan Seven Companies relocation issue, but without resolution. When the Miao Transport Envoy came to Yangzhou on the 16th, representatives from various circles went to petition him, but they were suppressed and dispersed by armed tax police, causing public outrage. The entire city went on strike, classes were boycotted, and work was stopped. Automobiles and ships were all suspended, and transportation was cut off. Students from various middle schools gathered to parade and demonstrate, and the atmosphere was unusually tense. Realizing the seriousness of the situation outside, Miao went to see Councilor Wang on the morning of the 17th and talked for three hours. After Wang repeatedly enlightened him, Miao deeply agreed with what Wang said and realized that he had been lacking in his own observations. He immediately signed a solution and met with representatives from various circles, voluntarily agreeing not to relocate the companies to the north. As a result, all parties were satisfied. In addition to the automobiles and ships resuming their schedules in the afternoon, all schools and shops resumed classes and business on the 18th. The salt crisis is expected to subside.

Disaster Victims in the Second District of Zhenjiang Petition 109

The Gaozi area in the second district of Zhenjiang suffered a severe drought this year. In addition, after the recent rains, the weather suddenly turned cold. The villagers in the various townships are crying out for food and clothing. Yesterday (the 17th) morning at around 10 a.m., over 400 people, men, women, old, and young, from 41 townships gathered and organized a petition group to come to Zhenjiang to petition the county government. They publicly elected four representatives, including Yang Xiangxian, to see County Magistrate Lai. They were met by Ruan Yanying, the head of the first section. The representatives stated two requests in their petition: first, to request emergency relief; second, to request the cancellation of taxes. Section Chief Ruan replied that he would submit the requests to the county magistrate and do his best to find a way to obtain funds from the Department of Finance. The representatives were satisfied and returned.

Second Investigation of Yang Zhaoti Case in Haimen 110

The former head of the seventh public security sub-bureau, Jing Bo, and patrol officer Miao Fengxiang, who shot and killed the thief Yang Zhaoti, also known as Xiao Yang, one patrolman, in the 19th year of the Republic, were sued by police officer Yu Jingyu to the Control Yuan. The Control Yuan forwarded the case to the High Court, which transferred it to the Shanghai District Court for investigation. The Shanghai Court conducted a second investigation the other day. The plaintiff, Yu Jingyu, and the defendant, Miao Fengxiang, were present. Jing Bo was absent due to illness. As a result of the interrogation, the court ordered Miao Fengxiang to be temporarily detained and summoned Jing Bo to appear for further questioning.

Gao Jinhua Silk Shop in Jiaxing Closes 111

Gao Jinhua Silk Shop in Jiaxing was a sole proprietorship established by Gao Zhonglan. It has been in business for over twenty years and has a good reputation in the business community. After the completion of the Jima Road in the North City, the shop purchased land and built a tall, foreign-style building there to expand its business. During the autumn sales of silk and cloth, the shop also occupied a favorable position in the business. However, after the Ziyuanzhuang and other three money shops declared liquidation and the Jiaxing Bank suspended payments, the shop was also affected by withdrawals from depositors. Although manager Chen Yongnian tried to maintain the business, it was difficult to manage. Therefore, the shop announced its closure on the 18th. However, it is said that the shop has not withdrawn most of the deposits from its depositors, and it also owes a considerable amount of money to creditors, totaling approximately 200,000 yuan. Therefore, it may be difficult to liquidate the shop.

Fire in Jianggan, Hangzhou Burns Old Woman to Death 112

A fire suddenly broke out at the Fusheng Tudi Temple in Tonghe Sanlangmiao, Jianggan, at around 4 p.m. the other day. The fire was quite fierce. Firefighters and various volunteer groups rushed to the scene to put out the fire. The fire was extinguished after about an hour of burning. After an investigation, it was discovered that an old woman who was unable to escape was burned to death. Her body was charred. The court was notified to send officials to inspect the body, and then it was placed in a coffin.

Special Report

Legislative Yuan, The Constitution of the Republic of China Passed on Third Reading (Continued) 113

Chapter IX Education

Article 143: The purpose of education in the Republic of China is to promote national spirit, cultivate national morality, train self-governing ability, enhance living skills, and create sound citizens.

Article 144: All citizens of the Republic of China shall enjoy equal opportunities for education.

Article 145: All public and private educational institutions nationwide shall be subject to national supervision and shall be obligated to promote the education policies established by the state.

Article 146: All school-age children from six to twelve years old shall receive basic education without tuition fees; details shall be determined by law.

Article 147: People who have exceeded school age but have not received basic education shall receive remedial education without tuition fees; details shall be determined by law.

Article 148: The establishment of national universities and national vocational schools should focus on regional needs to maintain equal opportunities for people in all regions to enjoy higher education and promote the balanced development of national culture.

Article 149: The minimum amount of educational funding shall be 15% of the total budget for the central government and 30% of the total budget for provinces, regions, counties, and cities. Independent educational funds established by law shall be guaranteed. Educational funding for impoverished provinces and regions shall be subsidized by the national treasury.

Article 150: Private schools with excellent performance shall be rewarded or subsidized.

Article 151: The education of nationals residing abroad shall be rewarded or subsidized.

Article 152: All public and private schools nationwide shall establish free and scholarship quotas to reward students with excellent academic performance and conduct who are unable to afford further education.

Article 153: School teachers and staff with excellent performance and long service shall be rewarded and guaranteed. Their seniority-based salary increases and pensions shall be determined by law.

Article 154: Academic and technological research and inventions shall be rewarded and protected.

Article 155: Historical sites and cultural relics related to history, culture, and art shall be protected and preserved by the state.

Chapter X Finance

Article 156: The division of financial revenue and expenditure systems for governments at all levels, as well as financial subsidies or assistance, shall be determined by law.

Article 157: The revenue and expenditure of governments at all levels shall be compiled into a general budget and a general final account once every fiscal year; the scope and procedures for their compilation shall be determined by law.

The compilation of the operational budgets and final accounts of publicly owned enterprises of governments at all levels may be regulated by separate laws; however, their net profits and losses shall still be incorporated into the general budget and general final account in accordance with the law.

For long-term construction projects, governments at all levels may set up continuing appropriations in accordance with the law, but their budgets shall still be incorporated into the general budget on an annual basis.

The general budget of governments at all levels shall not be established without legal procedures.

Article 158: The expenses stipulated in the budget shall be the maximum amount of expenditure and shall not be changed or exceeded without a supplementary budget according to law.

Governments at all levels may submit extraordinary budgets in one of the following circumstances: (1) emergency facilities for national defense or security; (2) major disasters; (3) urgent major projects.

Article 159: The following matters shall be resolved by the Legislative Yuan at the central level; those that can be regulated by separate regulations of provinces, regions, counties, or cities according to law shall be resolved by the respective legal organs: (1) the establishment of taxes, fees, fines, penalties, or other mandatory income, and changes in their collection rates; (2) the issuance of public bonds, the disposal of public property, or the conclusion of agreements that increase the burden on the public treasury; (3) the establishment or cancellation of public monopolies or other profit-making enterprises; (4) the granting or cancellation of monopolies, other exclusive rights, or privileges.

Provincial, regional, county, and city governments shall not raise foreign debts or directly utilize foreign capital without special permission from the law.

Article 160: All goods within the territory of the Republic of China shall be allowed to circulate freely and shall not be prohibited without law.

Customs duties are central government revenue and shall be levied only once when goods enter or leave the country.

Governments at all levels shall not levy goods transit taxes within the country; however, this shall not apply to usage fees levied on passing boats and vehicles due to improvements in waterways and roads.

The right to levy all taxes and levies on goods belongs to the central government and shall not be exercised without law.

Article 161: The financial organizations of all government agencies, including the treasury, accounting, and auditing departments, shall maintain their independence; details shall be determined by law.

Chapter XI Military Affairs

Article 162: The military forces of the Republic of China are established for national defense, belong to the central government, and have the duties of consolidating national power, defending the territory, resisting foreign aggression, and obeying laws and regulations.

Article 163: The military shall be based on a conscription system.

The obligations of citizens to participate in national defense shall be determined by law.

Article 164: The organization of the army, navy, and air force shall be determined by law.

Article 165: The President commands the army, navy, and air force. During peacetime, the power of command is exercised by the responsible department. During external defense wars, the President, with the consent of the Legislative Yuan, appoints a commander-in-chief to exercise the power of command; however, the commander-in-chief shall be dismissed immediately upon the end of the war.

Article 166: In the event that a foreign country first declares war on the country or attacks the country with force without declaring war, the President may issue orders for preemptive mobilization, defense, and martial law, and request subsequent ratification according to law.

Article 167: The entire country shall be divided into garrison areas according to national defense needs; details shall be determined by law. Military region commanders shall not have provincial capitals as their permanent residence.

Article 168: Troops shall be stationed in national defense zones and shall not be mobilized except upon orders from the central government or in the event of an emergency, upon request for assistance from the provincial, regional, county, or city governments.

The aforementioned emergency measures shall be immediately reported to the central government by the provincial, regional, county, or city governments and the military region commanders.

Article 169: Military expenses shall be paid by the national treasury, and the amount and number of officers and soldiers shall be determined in the budget.

Military supplies shall be independent and managed by the national treasury in accordance with the law.

Article 170: Provincial, regional, county, and city governments shall not organize troops, establish military educational institutions, or establish ordnance manufacturing plants.

Matters of provincial, regional, county, and city security shall be determined by law.

Article 171: Active military personnel shall not interfere in politics and shall not express political views.

Article 172: Active military personnel shall not concurrently hold administrative office.

Article 173: The exercise of military adjudication power and the organization of military adjudication organs shall be determined by law.

Chapter XII Supplementary Provisions

Article 174: The term "law" in the Constitution refers to laws passed by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the President.

Article 175: Laws that conflict with the Constitution are invalid.

Orders that conflict with the Constitution are invalid.

Article 176: The interpretation of the Constitution shall be made by the Judicial Yuan.

Article 177: The Constitution shall not be amended except by a proposal of one-fourth or more of all representatives of the National Assembly, the attendance of two-thirds or more, and the resolution of two-thirds or more of the representatives present.

Proposals to amend the Constitution shall be announced by the proposers one year before the meeting of the National Assembly.

Article 178: This Constitution shall take effect from the date of its promulgation.

Local News

American Journalist Delegation Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning 114

A Group of Seven Will Return to the United States Tonight Aboard the Ryuta Maru

The Drummonds Travel to Manila for Inspection

Excellent Impression of Our Country, No Opinions Expressed During Travel

The American press delegation, previously invited by the Japanese Press Association to tour Japan and inspect various parts of the Northeast, part of the delegation returned to Japan directly to return to their country, and another part, entered the customs to visit Peiping, stayed for six days, and arrived in Shanghai by the Peiping-Shanghai through train at eight o'clock yesterday morning, and decided to board the Ryuta Maru of the Nippon Yusen Kaisha tonight to return to the United States. Minister Kong held a tea party at his private residence at 4:30 yesterday afternoon to welcome them.

A Group of Seven Arrived in Shanghai in Transit 115

A part of the American press delegation, a total of nine people, traveled south by the Peiping-Shanghai through train. Except for the Drummonds of the Scientific Mirror, who got off in Beijing midway, the remaining seven people arrived in Shanghai by through train at eight o'clock yesterday morning and stayed at the Cathay Hotel on the Bund. They were Mr. and Mrs. Ping Tuo of the Chicago Daily, Mr. Robert of the St. Louis Star-Times and his son, Mr. and Mrs. Kemi Long of the San Francisco Public Opinion Newspaper, and Miss Tao Ping, a total of seven people. They are scheduled to tour the city and visit various places for the next two days and board the Ryuta Maru of the Nippon Yusen Kaisha tonight to return to the United States via Japan.

Mr. Drummond Goes to Bandit-Controlled Areas for Inspection 116

After the entire American press delegation finished inspecting the Northeast, they freely went to various places without being bound by the group. Mr. and Mrs. Drummond of the Scientific Mirror, who stayed in Beijing, were warmly received by the central authorities. They took the night train out of Beijing last night and are expected to arrive in Shanghai this morning. They will board a ship tomorrow to travel south to Manila to inspect the Philippines, and then return to the United States via Japan.

The American press delegation took a photo at the North Station, Mr. Kemi Long holding a hat (photographed by Shen Shi News Agency)

Minister Kong Hosted a Tea Party Yesterday 117

Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi specially held a grand tea party at his residence on Xiham Road at 4:30 yesterday afternoon. In addition to the seven members of the American press delegation, those present included the newly appointed Ambassador to Italy Liu Wendao and his wife, Minister to France Gu Weijun and his wife, former Minister to Sweden Zhu Changnian and his wife, Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Director of the Foreign Affairs Office Yu Ming, Section Chief Zhao Tiezhang, Liu Hongsheng, Bei Songsun, Tang Haian, Wen Yuqing, Zhao Jinqing, Guo Bingwen, and more than 100 reporters from Chinese and foreign newspapers. The host and guests parted happily at around six o'clock.

Kemi Long Talks About Tour Impressions 118

A reporter from this newspaper interviewed Mr. Kemi Long of the American press delegation at the Cathay Hotel yesterday morning. Mr. Kemi Long is the publisher of the San Francisco Public Opinion Newspaper. According to him, this trip was at the invitation of the Japanese press, and they traveled all over Japan and various parts of the Northeast, and met with celebrities from the government and the public. He was very grateful for their special and warm hospitality. The beautiful scenery and the places they visited were extremely pleasant. The progress of everything in Japan is even more worthy of praise.

Many False States and Bandits Visited Only Briefly 119

The reporter then asked about his views on the Northeast issue. Mr. Kemi Long said that the entire delegation visited the puppet state, and although they were warmly received by Zheng Xiaoxu and others, the time was too short and the visit was only brief. They were unable to comment on the Northeast issue, which is the root of the Sino-Japanese dispute, or express their opinions. However, based on the surface observations, the climate there is good and the products are abundant, but "bandits are rampant everywhere, and it is quite difficult to eliminate them for a while."

Minister Kong's tea party to entertain the American press delegation (photographed by Xu Tianzhang)

Excellent Impression of Visiting the Ancient Capital 120

Mr. Kemi Long continued to say that they stayed in Beiping for six days, visiting scenic spots. The ancient capital has an antique flavor and the scenery is quiet, elegant and magnificent, which makes people reluctant to leave. They were deeply grateful for the sincere hospitality of the Peiping authorities. It was also very pleasant to meet with celebrities such as Wang Zhengting, Ding Wenjiang, and Hu Shi. Dr. Wang Zhengting traveled south with them in the same car, and they talked about everything along the way, which was not lonely at all. They are scheduled to board the Ryuta Maru tomorrow night (i.e. tonight) and return to China via Japan, etc.

Liu Wendao Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 121

Mr. Liu was Promoted to Ambassador with Formal Appointment

The Appointment of the Italian Ambassador Will Be Announced Simultaneously

According to the Central News Agency, the newly appointed Ambassador to Italy, Mr. Liu Wendao, traveled to Beijing by night train from Shanghai on Sunday. He gave a lecture at the Central University on Monday. After completing his public affairs at 11 o'clock the night before, he took a night train to leave Beijing for Shanghai. He arrived at the North Station at 7:20 yesterday morning and went straight to his new residence on Shanzhong Road to rest. Mr. Liu was dusty and his right eye was slightly ill, so he went out to see a doctor at around 9 o'clock in the morning, and then returned to his residence to receive many guests and handle miscellaneous affairs. Mr. and Mrs. Liu went to the tea party and dinner of Kong Xiangxi, Deputy Dean of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, at 4:30 and 8 o'clock yesterday afternoon. The China Road Association also hosted a banquet for Mr. Liu at 7 o'clock last night.

Going to Hunan in a Few Days 122

Mr. Liu is scheduled to rest in Shanghai for a few days, and then he will take a boat with his wife to Wuhan and Changsha to visit old friends and return to his hometown of Wuxue to sweep the tombs. He will enter Beijing at the beginning of next month to attend the Fifth National Congress. As for the date of taking office, it will be postponed to mid-December.

As for the formal appointment, it will be announced simultaneously after the candidate for the Italian ambassador is decided. General Situation of Domestic and Foreign Economic Trade in the First Half of the Year 124

Published Yesterday by the International Trade Bureau

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, China's foreign trade was still sluggish in the first and second quarters of this year. Both exports and imports were lower than in previous years. The Shen Shi News Agency reporter interviewed Mr. He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, yesterday and received the trade statistics for the first half of the year from the bureau, which showed that imports decreased by 26% and exports decreased by 9%. A summary is provided below.

Document from the National Trade Bureau to the Ministry of Industry 125

The International Trade Bureau reported on the trade situation in the first half of this year and submitted a document to the Ministry of Industry, which read: "We would like to report that the trade situation in 1932 and 1933 has been reported in installments. The first and second quarters of this year have passed in a flash. During this period, China's foreign trade was still sluggish, and both imports and exports were lower than in the same period last year. Imports decreased by 26% and exports decreased by 9%. The degree of decline in imports was greater than that in exports, which is somewhat gratifying. As for trade commodities, in terms of exports, China's main commodities, such as raw silk, egg products, and tea, have seen a significant decline in foreign sales. Cotton goods and cotton yarn have also been lower than in previous years. Only furs, leather, wool, coal, and animal skins have been slightly active. It is evident that domestic production has not seen any recent development. In terms of imports, there is something gratifying, that is, the import of agricultural products and rice has suddenly shown a very sharp decline. Other main commodities, such as cotton cloth, kerosene, coal, paper, chemical products, sugar, ammonium sulfate, rayon, fish and shellfish, and seafood, have all decreased compared with the same period last year. Only the import figures for machinery and hardware have suddenly increased, which may be a sign that domestic industrial construction is gradually becoming concrete. Overall, the trade situation in the first and second quarters of this year is still declining, but the deficit in the two quarters has decreased by more than 170 million yuan compared with the same period last year due to the sharp decrease in imports. If the domestic situation can move towards a stable and well-off state in the future, it will not be difficult for industry and commerce to achieve prosperity together, and foreign trade may tend to be balanced. At the end of the first and second quarters of trade, we report on the situation. Please review and approve. Sincerely presented to Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry, He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau."

International Economy Slightly Stabilizes 126

The world economic panic, which began in 1929, has become increasingly severe. Until last year, due to the efforts of governments to seek relief, there were signs of improvement. In the first half of this year, the economies of various countries continued to move towards recovery. Although the progress was slightly slower due to the dangerous international political situation, the finances of various countries have improved compared to before, currencies have not entered a state of fierce war, and finance has been slightly stable. Industry and trade have seen significant increases. On the surface, the situation this year is more optimistic than last year. However, we must know that the panic policies currently implemented by various countries all contain inherent contradictions and are not enough to make the world's production and consumption match. Today's economic recovery is actually limited to the domestic affairs of various countries, and mostly occurs in countries that devalue their currencies. In these countries, workers have not initially received the benefits of recovery, and the actual wages earned are very low. Agriculture and the purchasing power of the people are declining and suffering even more losses. The public works programs carried out by the government have had little effect. In addition, the trade policies of various countries are quite conflicting, and the obstacles to world trade have not been reduced at all. Therefore, a true world economic recovery is not easy to talk about at this time.

Domestic Economy Declines Day by Day 127

In the first half of this year, although the economies of various countries showed signs of recovery, China's domestic economy remained the same as before, without any progress. Agricultural production is expected to be poor this year due to the drought in June. Industry has made little progress due to the weak purchasing power of the people and the influx of foreign goods. Finance is still in a state of imbalance. In addition, due to the upcoming implementation of American silver purchases, silver is flowing out of the country. In recent years, cash in China has been flowing from the interior to central cities, and now it is flowing from cities to foreign countries. If this continues, the national economy will inevitably suffer a major breakdown. Although there are one or two optimistic phenomena in other domestic finance, transportation, and shipping, overall, China's domestic economy this year is still in a state of recession.

Foreign Trade Becomes More Exhausted 128

This year, the world economy is still declining, the domestic economy is also in recession, and foreign trade is still in a state of slump, which goes without saying. In terms of total trade volume, the first quarter was 416,572,749 yuan, and the second quarter increased slightly to 421,821,801 yuan. If we analyze the export trade, both import and export figures were highest in January. On the export side, the net export value in January was 50,775,783 yuan. In February, the value of exports decreased sharply due to the fact that the old lunar new year period has historically been a slow month, with just over 38,350,000 yuan. In March and April, it increased slightly to around 41 million yuan. In May and June, it rose to more than 49 million yuan, but it still did not break the highest export figure in January in the first half of the year. Comparing the export figures for the first and second quarters, the second quarter was stronger. The total export value in the first quarter was 128.92 million yuan, while the second quarter reached 140.61 million yuan. On the import side, the net import value in January was 105.46 million yuan, 82.75 million yuan in February, and 99.42 million yuan in March. The total import value in the first quarter was more than 287.64 million yuan. The import value in April increased relatively, reaching 100.96 million yuan. The import value in May and June trended downward again, with 94.98 million yuan in May and 86.25 million yuan in June. The total import value in the second quarter was 282.2 million yuan, which was slightly lower than the import value in the first quarter by 5.44 million yuan. The total export value in the first half of this year was 269.54 million yuan, the import value was 569.84 million yuan, and the total foreign trade volume was 838.39 million yuan. The deficit in the first half of the year totaled 301.305 million yuan, a decrease of 173.33 million yuan compared to the deficit in the same period last year.
