Appeal from the Yarn Association 131

Yesterday, a Telegram Was Sent to the Executive Yuan and Ministries to Request a Revision of the Tariff

An Emergency Meeting Will Be Held Again on a Scheduled Date

The Shanghai Chinese Cotton Mill Association believes that the Ministry of Finance's plan to increase the unified tax on cotton yarn is of great importance to the future of the yarn industry. Therefore, it held a meeting of the Executive Committee yesterday afternoon and passed a telegram to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Cotton Control Committee. The details are recorded below.

Emergency General Meeting to Be Held on a Scheduled Date 132

The association held a meeting of the Executive Committee yesterday afternoon to conduct a detailed discussion. It was generally believed that the decline of the yarn industry has reached its extreme and cannot bear any further burdens. A general meeting should be convened to jointly discuss rescue methods. Therefore, it was decided to convene a national emergency general meeting of the Chinese yarn factory industry in Shanghai at 2:00 p.m. on the 28th of this month. The association has notified all Chinese yarn factories across the country to send representatives to participate in the meeting.

Tariff Revision Should Be Divided into Four Levels 133

The Chinese Yarn Mill Association sent a telegram to the Executive Yuan and Ministries, which read: "Greetings to President Wang of the Nanjing Executive Yuan, Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry, and Chairman Chen of the Shanghai Cotton Control Committee. Recently, the Ministry of Finance has suddenly proposed an increase in the unified tax on cotton yarn. Rumors are spreading, and the public is panicked. Since the implementation of the unified tax in our country's cotton textile industry, Chinese factories have suffered serious blows due to the poor tax rate levels. Recently, the situation has become even more precarious due to increased taxes on imported cotton and reduced taxes on cotton products. If the proposed tax increase is borne by consumers and has nothing to do with manufacturers, this statement may still be valid when rural areas are stable and sales are booming. However, in recent years, droughts and floods have occurred one after another, and rural areas have gone bankrupt. People are selling at a loss in order to seek a profit, and users are still unable to afford it. If prices are increased again, no one will be interested. The newly added tax is equivalent to increasing the burden on the factory and increasing losses. When manufacturers' losses deepen, they will inevitably be closed down. The income from the unified tax will disappear accordingly. Trying to alleviate an urgent need by sacrificing something essential will not solve the problem. Even if the government increases taxes in order to enrich the national treasury, it should follow the principles of taxation, seek a balance in burdens, and increase those that should be increased and reduce those that should still be reduced. For example, 4-count cotton yarn, which sells for about 100 yuan, is classified in the same level as 20-count cotton yarn, which sells for 170-180 yuan, and is subject to a heavy tax of 8 yuan and 58 cents. 60-count fine yarn, which is worth more than 400 yuan, is classified in the same level as 32-count fine yarn, which is worth 230-240 yuan, and is subject to a light tax of 11 yuan and 63 cents. The imbalance in the burden is so great. Chinese factories, which mostly spin coarse yarn, have suffered enormous losses. In recent years, factories have been declining day by day and eventually collapsing. The poor tax system is one of the main reasons for this. If we can take this opportunity to change the tariff to the four-level system of customs, reduce those that should be reduced and increase those that should be increased, factories will dare not disobey. If we still increase taxes according to the original two-level system, it is tantamount to fearing that Chinese factories will not perish quickly and encouraging them to perish together. We have always known that you are maintaining the industry with the utmost care. We earnestly ask you to consider the imminent danger of the factory industry, which is like a thread about to break. Please exempt cotton yarn from being increased, or differentiate between heavy and light and change the level of taxation, so as to prolong the life of the national factory. We are extremely eager to await your orders. The Chinese Yarn Mill Association respectfully asks."

Telegram from Tianjin Yarn Industry Appealing for Help 134

Tianjin Yarn Mill Industry Association,

Telegraphs: To Minister of Finance of Nanjing, Commissioner of Shanghai Customs, and Chairman of the Cotton Industry Control Committee: We have received a letter from the Chinese Yarn Mill Association stating that we have been verbally informed by the Commissioner of Customs that it is planned to increase the cotton yarn consolidated tax from November 1st. Upon hearing this, we were extremely shocked. The yarn industry has been in decline in recent years, reaching its lowest point, especially for yarn mills in Hebei and Tianjin. The existing yarn machines in Hebei can mostly only spin coarse yarn, and the woven products from coarse yarn can only be sold to farmers in rural areas and cannot be sold in large quantities in cities. Since the bankruptcy of rural areas in Hebei, the purchasing power is weak, and the sales of cotton yarn have been extremely scarce. Furthermore, due to the drastic changes in the East Provinces, a major sales market has been lost. As a result, the price of yarn has fallen drastically. The price obtained per bale is only enough to cover the cost of cotton and taxes, leaving no money for wages. If this loss continues to worsen and difficulties increase, even if the tax is not increased temporarily, the mills are already in imminent danger, and some mills have already reported shutdowns and cannot resume work. How can they bear the additional burden? Wouldn't they all close down one after another? If the yarn mills cease to exist, where will the yarn tax come from? If the source of tax revenue is lost, what is the benefit of increasing taxes? If it is said that the increased tax can be indirectly passed on to the users, we believe that this argument may be valid when sales are extremely strong. However, now that prices are being lowered to seek sales, users are still struggling to afford it. Where is there room for price increases? In addition to the Chinese Yarn Mill Association exhaustively stating the situation of factories nationwide, we would like to further explain the advantages and disadvantages of the situation in Hebei in detail. We humbly request that you consider the market conditions, continue to sympathize with the difficulties of businesses, cancel the previous proposal, and extend the lifeline of yarn mills. We would be extremely grateful. Sincerely, Tianjin Yarn Mill Industry Association.

Great China Rubber Factory Resolved to Resume Work Today 137

Unanimous Resolution Passed at Yesterday's Board of Directors Meeting

And Relief for Innocent Workers Affected

According to the Industry News Agency, the Great China Rubber Factory has been experiencing labor unrest since the 4th of this month, lasting for half a month. The factory has repeatedly received earnest mediation from party and government agencies and various domestic goods organizations. A special emergency meeting of the board of directors was convened at the office at 2 PM yesterday, attended by Yu Zhiqin, Du Yuesheng, Lin Kanghou, Shi Gengyin, Wu Zhesheng, Xue Fuji, Yuchi Xunzhi, Yu Xingben, Zhu Huiren, Jiang Binxian, Yu Jieru, Hong Nianzu, and others, totaling more than 20 people. Manager Xue Fuji first reported that recently, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Federation of Domestic Goods Factories, the Shanghai Machine Federation, the China National Products Maintenance Association, the Shanghai Citizens' Association for Promoting Domestic Products, and the Rubber Products Association of Domestic Goods have forwarded instructions from the Ministry of Industry and the Bureau of Social Affairs, urging the company to resume work as soon as possible to maintain the livelihoods of the majority of innocent workers, demonstrating the government and society's utmost concern for the industry. Moreover, more than 1,300 innocent workers at the factory jointly pleaded for an early resumption of work and requested relief during the suspension of work. All the directors and supervisors present unanimously passed the following resolutions: (1) Comply with the Bureau of Social Affairs' urging and resume work first to maintain the livelihoods of innocent workers. (2) Those who were arrested for violent acts have been punished by the court according to law, and those who have fled and have not been apprehended should be dismissed immediately. (3) Workers who participated in disruptive behavior before and after the event should be listed separately and reported to party and government agencies for dismissal according to law. (4) During this factory riot, more than 1,300 innocent workers who were paid by piecework were innocently implicated and are deserving of sympathy. Based on the requests from the inspectors and foremen of various departments for relief, permission is granted to provide appropriate subsidies. (5) Whether paid by monthly salary or piecework, contracts must be signed to ensure compliance. The company immediately reported to the Bureau of Social Affairs and scheduled to resume work today (the 19th) and requested that personnel be dispatched to supervise the process. The labor-management disputes of the past half-month have thus come to an end. It is reported that the factory suffered tangible losses of more than 20,000 yuan, while intangible losses are still being calculated.

The Establishment of the Stabilization Committee Will Still Require a Considerable Amount of Time 138

Yesterday, Minister Kong Called Banking Leaders for Talks

Authorities Should Strictly Prevent Private Smuggling of Silver

According to the Guowen News Agency, now that an export tax has been levied on silver, the authorities are discussing the second step with the banking community to organize a silver price stabilization committee. Yesterday afternoon, Bei Songsun of the Bank of China, Zhang Gongquan of the China Bank, Li Fusun of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Chen Guangfu of the Shanghai Bank, Song Zi Liang of the China Construction Silver Company, and others gathered at the Central Bank to talk with Minister of Finance and President of the Central Bank Kong Xiangxi and Vice President Chen Xing for about an hour before dispersing. Although the authorities denied that the talks were about the silver tax issue, it is generally expected that they were related to stabilizing the price of silver. According to another banking source, the Ministry of Finance's announcement of the silver export tax has aroused panic in various markets. Not only have the gold and securities markets risen steadily in recent days, but the flour and yarn markets have also risen sharply. Therefore, the establishment of a stabilization committee is imperative today. The content of Minister Kong's talks today is still unknown. Although foreign exchange is now listed by the Central Bank, foreign banks may still have problems with exchange rates in the future. At that time, the stabilization committee can be responsible for resolving these problems. Therefore, the establishment of this committee is like adding a buffer between foreign banks and the Central Bank, making everything easier to negotiate.

As for the committee's domestic mission, the greatest is to suppress and stabilize the price of silver in the domestic market. If the price of gold in the gold market is seen to be high, the committee will definitely take the method of selling it to suppress it. If the price is seen to be low, it will definitely buy it to raise it. With this key, the stabilization committee must have a strong fund. Without a fund of four to five hundred million, it cannot be used for circulation. Now that such a large fund is handled by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, it is really difficult to bear. Therefore, although the stabilization committee is desired, the date of its establishment may still require a considerable amount of time. Furthermore, because silver has been taxed for export, due to the increase in silver tax, there will definitely be more people who smuggle and evade taxes. This is something that must be paid attention to.

"Kneeling and Crying Group" Discovered in Shanghai Amid the Dumping of Foreign Goods 139

Specially Persuading Chinese People Not to Buy Foreign Goods

Aiming to Love the Country, Seeking Nothing Else

According to the Industrial News Agency, since foreign goods have been dumped in the interior of our country, our industry and commerce have plummeted, and economic panic has reached its extreme. However, the so-called modern men and women youths in cities all regard the use of foreign goods as fashionable, to the extent that they are not modern without wearing foreign goods. As a result, the sales of domestic goods have plummeted. In the past, patriotic people had organizations like the "Assassination Group," but their actions interfered with the law, so they were soon banned by the authorities. Recently, a "Kneeling and Crying Group" has suddenly been discovered in this city. Its members are only a few people who specialize in wandering on the road. When they see Chinese people buying foreign goods, they immediately step forward, kneel down, and plead to use domestic goods to save the country from danger. The reporter witnessed members of this "Kneeling and Crying Group" kneeling and pleading with a young girl on Fada Road, asking her not to buy foreign goods. When the reporter stepped forward to inquire about their names, they refused to answer and only said that they were aiming to love the country, promote domestic goods, and were seeking nothing else.

Page 10

Announcement of the General Assembly Declaration After the Closing of the National Child Welfare Conference 142

Judging of Exhibits Today

The National Child Welfare Leaders Conference held its general assembly in Shanghai this time. Leaders of child welfare undertakings from all over the country came to Shanghai to attend, opening a new era in China's child welfare field. The grand occasion of the past few days has been recorded in previous reports. The China Wireless Electric Research Society specially installed a sound amplification machine in the grand auditorium of the New Asia Hotel, which was especially convenient for the general assembly's speeches and the statements of various representatives. Bingxun Shorthand School sent many students to serve as recorders for the general assembly. All the speeches from all parties were recorded in detail. Wang Kai Photography Studio also volunteered to take photographs, and detailed materials will be available for future compilation of reports. As for the general assembly declaration, after the general assembly approved the principles, the drafting committee members and the general assembly secretariat made careful revisions for days, and it is now published as follows:

General Assembly Declaration 143

The foundation of national salvation lies in education, and the education of children is the most fundamental of all. Not only should poor and destitute children be given adequate education, but even wealthy families should make every effort to provide children with a complete education, so as to treat everyone equally and seek the happiness of equal education. At this time of national crisis, rural bankruptcy, and the lack of education and support for children are common. We should follow Confucius's meaning of "caring for the young and not only loving one's own children" and pay attention to the work of child welfare. In view of this, the China Child Welfare Association, based on Sun Yat-sen's Construction Program, Article 11, on childcare, has been working hard for the past six years and has drawn up a five-year plan for relief, education, sanitation, and various methods to protect children, with a clear outline and detailed items, hoping to achieve success. In addition, because the child welfare organizations in various provinces, counties, districts, and cities across the country have not been linked and unified, the National Child Welfare Leaders Conference was held from October 10th to 13th, 23rd year of the Republic of China. A total of 129 representatives from 15 provinces were invited to participate in the conference, and 95 proposals were submitted, which is an unprecedented achievement. The matters that have been passed have been handed over to the Child Welfare Association for execution. From now on, all our comrades, each will exhaust their intelligence and strive for practicality, without fearing difficulties, so that the existing child welfare organizations can be transformed and perfected to meet the scientific methods of education. In places where child welfare organizations have not been established, they must also be gradually promoted in accordance with the resolutions. In general, it can be divided into five categories: 1. Education: Do not be satisfied with the child welfare purpose of relief and nurturing, but also pay attention to the perfection of education. In addition to ordinary children, efforts must also be made to transform bad children, remedy disabled children, and advise and correct other abused children and families with various defects. The training of parents and teachers is also part of child welfare work. We must ensure that no child in the country is left unattended and that they can enjoy healthy and complete education, so as to achieve the development of children's physical and mental well-being. The strength of the country and the strengthening of the nation depend on this. 2. Relief: Do not be satisfied with sporadic relief and each taking in orphaned and poor children to avoid them ending up in ditches. We must unite the national forces to establish various specialized schools and factories, teach according to their aptitude, so that there are no unteachable children and no unachievable occupations, so as to block the source of poverty and cut off the cause of depravity. Even for wealthy children who drop out of school or whose parents indulge them in wandering, they should be advised, replace their bad habits with proper entertainment, and teach them to save money to avoid immorality. 3. Sanitation: The mortality rate of children in our country is higher than in Eastern and Western countries due to ignorance of methods of raising children hygienically. We should strive to promote and instill common sense, enforce prevention, strictly ban unqualified doctors, reward health, and conduct more competitions. Teaching and work that are not conducive to children's physical and mental health should be prohibited to protect children's health. 4. Legal Protection: The Chinese people still ignore many cruel and inhumane customs, such as drowning girls, abusing maids, destroying child brides, abandoning illegitimate children, and selling prostitutes. We urgently need to conduct strict investigations, impose severe punishments, and request the government to formulate children's laws and establish special children's courts to replace punishment with education so that they can reform themselves and respect humanity. This is also an important mission of our association. 5. Association Organization: Now, in order to revitalize and improve the existing child welfare organizations across the country in a short period of time and to establish a greater number of new organizations and implement dozens of new undertakings, it is impossible to achieve success without a strong general association that unites the organizations and directs and assists them from above. However, the funding is huge, and it cannot be covered by private donations. We hope that the government will expand its embrace, remember the teachings of protecting the infant, and allocate funds for permanent assistance, promotion, protection, and assistance at any time. We also hope that comrades across the country will be of one mind and work together, and carefully abide by the oath to do our best to relieve and educate the children of China today, to build the foundation of the family and society in the near future, and to build the foundation of the nation and country in the long run. This is also what the government will be happy to see. Next year is Children's Year. We hope that our colleagues will work hard in the child welfare industry, assist the government, and follow the progress of educating and nurturing children in the world's powers. We especially hope that our compatriots across the country will rise to the occasion and correct the shortcomings of this association. This declaration is hereby made in the hope that it will be made public.

Judging Exhibits 144

The child welfare organizations from various places participating in the Child Welfare Conference exhibition include the Xiangshan Children's Home and 42 orphanages in Henan, Jiangxi, Hankou, Hunan, Hubei, Shaanxi, etc. The general assembly publicly resolved to appoint Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaofan, Qu Jinqing, Ding Shujing, Zhu Lide, Zhu Shaoyang, Lin Kanghou, Qu Wenliu, Chen Liting, and other nine people to form a judging committee to judge the merits. The judging committee will hold a judging session at the Zhabei People's Education Center at 3 PM today to award certificates. It is heard that if the exhibitors wish to leave the exhibits for permanent exhibition as a memento, the China Child Welfare Association will be responsible for their safekeeping.

Provincial Branches 145

After the closing of the National Child Welfare Conference, representatives from various provinces have set out on their return journey. Representatives from Shaanxi Province, Zhang Ziyi and Huang Zuozhao, representatives from Henan Province, Li Zhuting and Wang Congzhou, and representatives from Hubei Province, Li Jiahe, etc., all expressed that after returning to their provinces, they would immediately begin contacting local agencies, organizations, and child welfare comrades to start organizing branches and actively prepare. Representatives from Peiping, Wang Xizhi, and representatives from Nanjing, Li Yaodong and Ma Wenhuan, etc., expressed that after returning to their provinces, they would immediately convene the members of the original child welfare organizations to strengthen their forces and promote child welfare work.

Zhang Tinggui, Comprador of Sin Fung Company, Accused of Raping a Young Girl 146

The Victim Recently Gave Birth to a Daughter and Has Not Yet Recovered

The Judge Paid Attention to Whether She Was Over Sixteen Years Old

Zhang Tinggui is a local, 38 years old, and works as a comprador in Sin Fung Company at 117 Sassoon House, Nanjing Road Bund, Shanghai. He is fond of women. He had a local woman surnamed Song, 53 years old, living at 62 Gaofuli, Rue Notre Dame, French Concession. She had two daughters, the elder named Wanhua and the younger named Fudi. On October 17 of last year, she was lured by Zhang to Room 502 of the Huaan Building and raped. He induced her with sweet words not to make a sound. In November, he raped her again. On December 4th, he raped her again in Room 44 of the Yipinxiang Hotel. Fudi became pregnant. Because she was not yet sixteen years old at the time, her mother, Song, noticed that her abdomen was gradually swelling and became suspicious. After questioning her, she learned the truth. Because what was done could not be undone, she tolerated it. Zhang Tinggui ignored Fudi and cut off contact. Song lost in the first trial and appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court. At 3 PM yesterday afternoon, Judge Yu presided over the first criminal court. Both sides arrived on time with their lawyers. The lawyer representing the appellant Shen Song first stated that the appellant Shen Song was unable to appear in court due to illness. The victim, Shen Fudi, gave birth to a daughter on the 11th of this month (October) after being raped and impregnated by the appellee Zhang Tinggui. She is not yet a month old and has not recovered, so she cannot appear in court. She requested the court to grant an extension and bring the newborn child to the court after the victim has recovered to request an examination of the child's face and blood to determine whether it is compatible with the appellee Zhang Tinggui to determine whether the appellee committed the crime. Judge Yu then said that the victim did not need to appear in court. The key to this case is whether the victim was under sixteen years old. The lawyer representing the appellant then stated that the victim was born on the sixth day of the twelfth lunar month in the sixth year of the Republic of China, the year of the Snake. There is a written record in the original trial. She was not yet sixteen years old when the appellee raped her in the Huaan Building, and the appellee cannot present any evidence to the contrary. Therefore, the appellee should be held liable under Article 240, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. After Judge Yu questioned Zhang Tinggui and the lawyers on both sides argued for a long time, he announced the end of the debate in this case and scheduled the verdict for 2 PM on the 23rd of this month.

The Doumu Pavilion of the Guandi Temple in Ximen Collapsed 148

Injuring Eight Guests Surnamed Ye

Ye Apei, a local resident living at 25 Yongnianli, Chengdu Road, works at the Commercial Press. Yesterday was the birthday of his ancestors, so he was introduced by a friend surnamed Chen living at 10 Anlefang, Penglai Road in this city to host a banquet at the Guandi Temple in Ximen, booking seven tables of vegetarian dishes at six yuan per table. However, there were as many as six families using the temple yesterday, and the Ye family was arranged in the east hall, on the second floor of the three-bay Doumu Pavilion. The downstairs was occupied by a Tong family. At 3:10 PM, Ye's relatives and friends took their seats together. Just as they were about to start eating, they suddenly heard a strange sound from the floor. In an instant, with a loud bang, the central part completely collapsed, injuring eight guests, including Hou Chaogen (28 years old, back broken), Liu Rujin (22 years old, right foot), Chen Jisheng (35 years old, shoulder and right foot), Zhou Bofa (34 years old, face), Shen Binlin (30 years old, head), and Wen Luping (32 years old, head). The above six people were sent to Renji Hospital. Ji Zhenggao and Wu Ruda were sent to Shanghai Hospital. At that time, the monk in charge of the temple, Daming, reported to the Chenxiangge Sub-bureau, who immediately sent many police officers to investigate the cause of the collapse. The east hall was a newly built building, and the wood inside was unusually large, so there was no reason for it to collapse. It was found that there were two horizontal girders in the central floor. Because the end of one of the horizontal beams was carved with patterns about an inch deep, and the tenon was only about an inch deep, the force was too great, the patterns were destroyed, the girder came loose, and the entire structure collapsed. Fortunately, the Tong family downstairs had finished their banquet and left only a few minutes before the disaster occurred, otherwise the consequences would have been unimaginable.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Cables Request to Correct the Ganzhou County Post Office's Increased Fees for Registered Items 153

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce cabled the Ministry of Communications yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Communications in Nanjing: On the 17th of this month, we received a joint letter from the Ganzhou County Domestic Piece Goods Trade Association, Foreign Goods Trade Association, and Dyeing Trade Association, stating that Ganzhou City is an important town in southern Jiangxi, where merchants gather and ships converge. In the past, goods were mostly transported from Shanghai and Hankou. However, since the bandit communists caused disturbances and the Gan River was blockaded, merchants in Shanghai purchase piece goods and other goods, mostly sending them by parcel post. The Ganzhou County Post Office, citing the increased number of parcels and the high cost of transporting them by rickshaw, requires recipients of parcels from Shanghai and Hankou via Ji'an to pay an additional two 'simple fees,' while parcels routed through Guangzhou require recipients to pay an additional one 'simple fee' before they can pick up their goods. Parcels sent directly from Guangzhou to Ganzhou are not subject to additional fees, which is particularly puzzling, undermining the uniformity of the postal service and increasing the suffering of merchants. The merchants Liu Yixiang, Zeng Tangcheng, Wang Xiangkun, and Xiao Xintian of the association presented a petition to the Nanjing Ministry of Communications, Shanghai Postal Administration, and Jiangxi Postal Administration in Shanghai in 1933, requesting that the fees be abolished, which was duly recorded. The Shanghai Postal Administration issued Approval No. 2618, stating that the postage for parcels sent by post is determined according to the distance, traffic conditions, and the amount of freight paid. Therefore, when traffic conditions change in various places, resulting in increased freight costs, the respective administrations may, according to the circumstances, charge the sender or receiver half, one, or several 'simple fees' to cover the costs. If freight costs in Ganzhou return to normal, the additional fees will be reduced or abolished. The merchants' parcels to Ganzhou must be routed through Guangzhou for delivery, resulting in high freight costs. The Ganzhou County Post Office's charging of an additional 'simple fee' has been approved and is not inappropriate. However, in the future, when freight costs decrease, the additional fee should be reduced or abolished. We have already instructed the Jiangxi Postal Administration to pay attention to this matter and inform them of this decision. According to reports, the Ganzhou-Geng and Ganzhou border highways have been opened to traffic, and long-distance buses can directly reach Shaozhou and Nanchang. Transportation is convenient and fast, and mail is transported entirely by buses, so freight costs should be reduced. The previous reason for charging additional fees due to rickshaw transportation no longer exists. Since freight costs have returned to normal, the additional 'simple fee' should be abolished to comply with postal regulations. However, the Ganzhou County Post Office is violating postal regulations, disregarding the difficulties of merchants, and extorting money for its own benefit, continuing to charge the fees, which is illegal. If this continues, the merchants in Ganzhou will undoubtedly suffer, and the goods from Shanghai and Hankou entering southern Jiangxi will also be greatly affected."

"In addition to requesting that the Jiangxi Postal Administration order the abolition of the fees, we are submitting this document to your esteemed ministry for review and request that you, based on the situation, forward it for approval and abolition to alleviate the difficulties of merchants. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce respectfully petitions. We have investigated that the postal service charges postage for parcels according to regulations. Additional postage fees from the sender or receiver should only be charged when local conditions change, causing an increase in postal transportation costs. The so-called change in local conditions only refers to traffic obstructions and the postal service needing to detour, and there is no other reason to increase freight costs. Now, goods from Shanghai and Hankou entering southern Jiangxi have very convenient transportation, and freight costs have actually decreased, so the local post office's continued collection of postage fees from recipients is completely unreasonable. Based on the above, we respectfully request that your esteemed ministry order the correction of this situation to alleviate the difficulties of merchants. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce respectfully prays."

Public Concession's Sanitary Conditions Last Month 160

Report from the Municipal Council's Health Officer for September: The prevailing diseases this month were intestinal diseases, more so than dysentery. Although these diseases are not as severe as cholera, they still require urgent research. However, no results have yet been obtained. It is unlikely that there will be a reduction until more effective management of food preparation and milk supply is achieved.

Malaria has also become more prevalent recently. One of the reasons is that residents are gradually moving to quieter areas, making them more susceptible to mosquito bites. Also, mosquitoes have become more numerous in the central area in the past two years. This is because the newest buildings are often built on basements, and the gaps inside the basements become breeding grounds for mosquitoes, which are extremely difficult to eradicate. This matter is currently being studied, but this is a new problem, and few countries have paid attention to it, so there is a lack of reference material.

The mortality rate this month remains low. Aside from the above, the infectious disease situation is generally normal. There are no more cases of cholera, so the injection vehicles were changed to smallpox vaccination on October 1. The total number of people vaccinated this season was only 249,106. Despite strong publicity efforts, people are not paying attention because cholera is rarely seen. The open-air swimming pools closed at the end of September. The number of visitors this year exceeded previous years. The increase in ticket prices was unavoidable, but as a result, undesirable elements were reduced, and the pools were not too crowded.

Physical examinations for schoolchildren have now officially begun. A lot of material has been obtained. Once the initial work is completed, appropriate action can be taken to meet urgent needs.

The birth rate for foreigners this month was 14.54 per thousand. The number of Chinese births reported was 298, of which 241 were residents of the Concession. As for deaths, the most common causes among Chinese were tuberculosis, typhoid fever, dysentery, and gastroenteritis.

The medical laboratory performed 3,387 tests this month, of which 542 had formal reactions. 179 food samples were inspected, of which 32 did not meet standards. 80 people sought treatment at the rabies clinic, and 9 of them came from outside the city.

The Chinese Isolation Hospital admitted 55 people last month, but this month the number increased to 74. 12 people died. 20 people were admitted due to diphtheria, which was the largest number. There were no cases of smallpox. Several people requested admission to the mental hospital, but they could not be admitted because there was no room.

The average daily milk production was 29,310 pounds, an increase of over 7% compared to last month. The results of the milk sample inspections showed that 4 samples did not meet chemical standards and 22 did not meet bacterial standards. Two employees were sent to court and fined for transporting milk without a license. The supply of meat was generally normal. The number of pigs slaughtered increased significantly due to the Mid-Autumn Festival, increasing by 14.4% compared to last month. The waste meat disposal facility disposed of 56,899 pounds of meat.

The work of the cleaning division, in addition to injections, has extended the date for fly and mosquito prevention. Well water disinfection has also been extended to the fall to prevent intestinal diseases. There have been many complaints about the nuisance of soot to neighbors, and most of these cases have been effectively handled, but there are one or two cases that are too big and are being considered. October 18, 1934.

The Qinyuan Village Drug Manufacturing Organization Was Highly Organized 161

Workers in Each Department Were Not Allowed to Interact

The Product Was the Extremely Toxic Heroin

Three Criminals Have Been Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

Cai Bicheng, a Sichuanese who had resigned as a county magistrate in Sichuan Province, brought his family to Shanghai and resided at No. 24 Qinyuan Village, Xinzha. He also leased the newly built four-story building at Nos. 175-177 Avenue Haig from the Dayao Construction Company on Museum Road to establish a morphine factory. On Double Ten Day, a fire broke out due to careless refining by workers. The workers in the factory fled together, and only three workers, Gong Baochang, Miao Zhangcai, and Gong Wenhu, were arrested. Cai heard the news at his residence that day and also abandoned his home with his family and belongings and fled. The Xinzha police station arrested Gong and the other two the next day and sent them to the First Special District District Court for questioning and detention. Judge Liu Yugui personally went to the scene to investigate the situation, as reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the drugs left in the factory after the fire have been tested in detail by the Municipal Council's Chemical Laboratory and identified as heroin, which is more toxic than morphine. However, it was only in the preliminary stage of production, so it was still in a sandy state. If it were further refined in the second step, it could become pure heroin. There are currently 304 pounds of this crude heroin, which is of considerable value at current prices. In addition to the three employees arrested, Wang Bingfu, Xu Ajin, Hu Yunqi, Liu Zhifen, and a Mr. Ren and a Mr. Wang escaped, along with the factory owner Cai Bicheng, for a total of seven people. Among them, Mr. Wang and Mr. Xu held the most important positions. Mr. Wang was the one who leased the house from Dayao, and Mr. Xu was the foreman. Yesterday morning, Judge Liu held a hearing, ordering Detective Tang Jian and Detective Lu Gendi to bring the three defendants, Gong Baochang, etc., to court for questioning. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, described the case and requested that the defendants be punished in accordance with Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law. He also requested that arrest warrants be issued for the fugitives. The court then questioned the three defendants, Gong, etc. However, none of them revealed anything about the factory's manufacturing situation, saying that they were all introduced to the factory by Xu Ajin and were assigned to the fourth floor to put wet wool into glass bottles, put them in pots, and bake them in the stove. When they were dry, they sent them to the third floor to be received by Xu Ajin. Those who worked on the fourth floor were not allowed to go to the third floor without permission, and those who worked on the third floor were not allowed to go to the fourth floor. The boundaries were strict, like a chasm. Judge Liu said that although the three of them joined the drug manufacturing group because they were tempted by others, if they could repent in time and confess the secrets of the factory in detail without concealment, they could be leniently treated. Therefore, he repeatedly instructed them to confess the truth. However, Gong and the others did not confess the working situation of how they produced the drugs in court. Judge Liu then announced the verdict: Gong Baochang, Miao Zhangcai, and Gong Wenhu were sentenced to six months of fixed-term imprisonment for continuously assisting in the manufacture of opium substitutes. The seized crude heroin and other raw materials, as well as all equipment, were confiscated. The car used to transport opium was also confiscated, and the wool was burned. The case can be said to be over. Cai Bicheng and the other seven fugitives are now wanted, and they will be dealt with separately when they are arrested.

Representative of Western Shipping Companies in Pudong Requests Supervision of Garbage Disposal 164

Xing Zhigang, a representative of Western shipping companies in Pudong, yesterday submitted a document to the Shanghai Municipal Government, stating:

Regarding the dumping of garbage in the Pudong area, which obstructs waterways, it is earnestly requested that the Health Bureau and Public Security Bureau be ordered to strictly prohibit such activity to preserve the commercial port. The Huangpu River serves as the main waterway connecting Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, free of reefs or shallows. Large ships from Dengzhou, Laizhou, Fujian, Guangdong, and foreign import merchant vessels can navigate with confidence and without hindrance. This is why Shanghai has earned the reputation as a world-renowned commercial port, and rightfully so. However, in recent years, the city and the British and French concessions have had difficulty finding locations to dispose of garbage. Land was purchased in the shallows near Longhua Mouth for dumping. However, those contracted to transport the garbage are all commercial business and the contract prices are harsh. As such, the hired laborers are unwilling to diligently unload the garbage. Instead, they dump it into the Huangpu River progressively as the tide rises south of Gaochang Temple. Heavy items such as bricks, tiles, stone chips, and coal sand sink immediately upon being dumped, leaving no trace. As for lighter, floating materials like rice straw and firewood, they float south to Tangkou with the high tide during major floods, accumulating and stagnating along both banks of the Huangpu River, obstructing waterways. It is believed that the Huangpu River is crucial to Shanghai's transportation and commercial development. Currently, in the southern Shanghai area, both banks of the Huangpu River are gradually being filled, while muddy currents and sand are continuously accumulating. Moreover, boatmen also dump garbage into the Huangpu River. With daily accumulation, it is feared that transportation will be obstructed by shallows, and the future consequences are unimaginable. Therefore, not daring to act presumptuously, this humble request is submitted, earnestly imploring your esteemed office to review and approve it and promptly instruct the Health Bureau and Public Security Bureau to closely inspect and supervise the loading and unloading of garbage along the route. Also, during minor floods and night tides, stop the boats from sailing to avoid dumping under the cover of night, thereby preserving the commercial port. The undersigned would be deeply grateful.

Lumber Industry Resolves Method for Converting Foreign Pine to Market Scale 165

Indicate the length of the market scale under the original size.

The Shanghai Lumber Industry Association believes that since the promulgation of the new system of weights and measures, there have been considerable obstacles to the sale of foreign pine in the industry. This is because foreign pine comes from Europe, America, Russia and elsewhere, and its scale of measurement is cut according to English feet when manufactured. This is not like the yardage of cloth, which can be measured and calculated by merchants at any time. For example, if there is a piece of foreign pine that is 16 English feet long, 12 inches wide, and 2 inches thick, it has already been sawn into lumber. Buyers and sellers trade according to the original scale. There is no room for change or expansion on either side. The members of the association, in order to respect the national system, have repeatedly consulted with foreign firms, requesting that foreign pine sold to China be sawn according to Chinese legal standards of measurement in the future. According to the foreign firms, the annual sales of European and American foreign pine are very large, and those sold to China account for less than one-tenth of the total. Their sawing machines and lumber scales are all manufactured to suit the English foot. If China wants them to change the sawing and change the scale, it is difficult to do so in reality. After repeated discussions, the association decided to calculate and price according to the original scale, intending to indicate the size of the Chinese market scale under the English foot scale, and calculate it using the "four-in-five-out" method for the convenience of transactions. The industry association has reported this method to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting that it be forwarded to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs for record.

Xinhua Village Successfully Constructed 166

Land prices on West Physical Education Association Road soar

Since the Xinhua Bank constructed Xinhua Village on West Physical Education Association Road in this city, the price of land in the surrounding area has been rising successively, reaching more than 6,000 taels per mu. As a result, some landowners along West Physical Education Association Road are waiting for a good price to sell, while others are starting to build houses. In addition, the road is a major thoroughfare connecting the concession and the city center, with frequent traffic and increasing activity. It is rumored that the site of the former National Shanghai College of Commerce across from the village is also planned to be rebuilt with new houses. Therefore, prosperity is imminent in the near future. It is said that Xinhua Bank did not consider the issue of profit when proposing Xinhua Village, due to its complete facilities (such as schools, shops, vegetable markets, children's parks, and tennis courts, etc.) and low selling prices. The prices were completely based on cost. However, after the increase in tariffs, the price of building materials has doubled. Since the bank had made a declaration earlier that it would not change the selling price before December of this year, it has made many sacrifices. It is now said that after December, the bank will consider increasing the price of construction, hoping to reduce the sacrifices slightly. Therefore, the selling price of the village may change in the future. It is also said that one of the four houses completed before the exhibition has already been sold, and people are contacting the other three houses every day, fearing that after the price changes, it will be difficult to obtain such affordable housing and excellent environmental areas.

Impersonating Mechanics, Stealing Electric Meters from Thirteen Homes 169

Detectives Uncover and Capture

Receiver of Stolen Goods Detained Simultaneously

Recently, shops and residents in the Nanshi area have been frequently targeted by individuals impersonating employees of the electric company, claiming to repair electric lights and meters, but in reality, replacing good meters with faulty ones and stealing the good meters. At the time, the shops believed them to be genuine, so those whose meters were stolen include: (1) Du Shunxing Garden, opened by Du Deqing at 452 Liyuan Road; (2) The home of Wen Xiaofeng at 9 Zhonghua Lane, Zhonghua Road; (3) Wanshunxing Clothing Store, opened by Jin Ruilin at 283 Xinqiao Road; (4) Gu Chaoqing's tiger stove at 28 Dapu Road; (5) Dong Mingde's home at 1449 Xietu Road; (6) Xue Haitao's home at 1294 Xietu Road; (7) Wang Jinbao's home at 18 Wuyun Lane, Xuxie Road; (8) Jin Guisheng's home at 370 Manufacturing Bureau Road; (9) Guan Rongxing's copper shop at 257 Manufacturing Bureau Road; (10) Hu Jingqi's home at 391 Huimi Road; (11) Cheng Yushu's home at 216 Menghua Street inside Ximen; (12) Shen Shunji's home at 233 Xinma Road, Yuyingtang, Zhabei, totaling thirteen households. The victims reported the incidents to Lu Bohong, General Manager of the China Electric Company, who in turn reported to Lu Ying, Captain of the Detective Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, requesting officers to investigate and apprehend the criminals. It is now known that Captain Lu dispatched Detective Leader Gao Wansheng, leading detectives Cao Baolin, Shi Yongquan, etc., to take charge of the investigation. Until noon the day before yesterday, they discovered that the meter thief was stealing an electric meter at the home of Zhang Hongji at 2 Zhangjiabang, Xinqiao Road, Nanshi. They uncovered the crime on the spot and arrested the thief. After interrogation, the thief confessed that he was Shi Liangyu, from Shaoxing, residing at 38 Luban Road, Nanshi. He used to work at the Gaochang Temple Arsenal, but is now unemployed and unable to make a living. Therefore, he purchased broken electric meters at low prices from various secondhand stalls, impersonating a mechanic to steal good meters, admitting to stealing from thirteen households, totaling thirteen electric meters, which he sold to Wang Changyi, a Jiangbei native who runs the Changji secondhand store at 189 Baoshan Lane, Pingjili Road, French Concession. The team then escorted the suspect Shi, together with detectives from the French Concession police station, to the address to continue the investigation, arresting Wang Changyi, the receiver of stolen goods. After interrogation, Wang made cunning excuses, refusing to confess the truth. Yesterday morning, both were sent to the Third Section for legal proceedings.

Children's Welfare Association Uncovers Human Traffickers 170

Li Bingyan, a staff member of the Protection Department of the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association, recently discovered that Wang Yueying (20 years old, from Huzhou) and Li Pu (49 years old, from Suzhou, resident of Sande Lane) of 2 Chunyuan Lane, Jiumudi, are suspected of human trafficking. He immediately reported to the Chairman of the Committee, requesting the Municipal Public Security Bureau to assist in the arrest. Director Wen ordered the Laobeimen Police Station under his jurisdiction to assist Staff Member Li in arresting Wang Yueying and Li Pu at 9:10 a.m. yesterday, as well as Wang's husband, Wen Qiusheng (35 years old, from Guangdong), their adopted daughter Zhaodi (7 years old, from Shanghai), and Li Pu's adopted daughter Yang Huizhen (17 years old, from Suzhou), and related person Lu Zhenting (59 years old, from Suzhou), and brought them to the station for verification. After interrogation by Station Chief Shen, Wang Yueying and Wen Qiusheng confessed that they bought the seven-year-old girl Zhaodi two weeks ago for sixty yuan through a middleman to be their adopted daughter. As for Yang Huizhen, they claimed that she was bought by their former domestic helper Li Pu. According to Li Pu, Yang Huizhen was purchased from Yang Yi in Suzhou on August 26 for six hundred yuan, with Lu Zhenting acting as a middleman, to be her adopted daughter because she was old and had no children to rely on. According to Lu Zhenting, Yang Huizhen was entrusted to him by a monk named Xia to act as a middleman. As the case involves the buying and selling of human beings, which is against the law, it is to be transferred to the General Bureau for legal proceedings.

Yu Ying, Captain of the Detective Team of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, stationed in the West Shanghai area, dispatched Detective Leaders Wu Kezhong and Cao Chuqiao. After reporting to Director Wang, they supervised detectives Zhang Wenbin, Zhong Xuehuai, Zang Nai, Zhang Shaoming, Shi Yulin, etc. to first go to 3 Guide Lane and arrest Wang Er, Zhang Jinyuan, Hu Yongxiang, and Tang Zhangshi, along with a package of red pills, and took them to the bureau. Then, they went to 3507 and 3517 Nanyinghua Lane, arresting Ma Guoshi and Zhai Zhangshi, and brought back 87 red pills as evidence to the bureau. After separate interrogations by bureau officers, they were sentenced to be held in custody and transferred to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Patrolling Officers Encounter Child Abduction Case and Arrest Suspects 172

Six-year-old Zhang Xiaojiang Abducted

At around 3 p.m. the day before yesterday, patrolling officers from the Putuo Road police station in West Shanghai noticed a woman carrying a boy of about six or seven years old, crying incessantly. The woman looked panicked and was trying to drag the child away. The officers, suspicious of the situation, immediately took them to the police station. After questioning by the police chief, it was revealed that the woman's name was Hu Liu, 24 years old, from Anhui, residing in a lime kiln in Xiaoshadu. The child's name was Zhang Xiaojiang, 6 years old, and was abducted by his neighbor, Li Li, who instructed Hu to send the child to Ling Kebing's house at 230 Baike Road, which specializes in selling children, with the intention of trafficking him. As the incident occurred in the Chinese territory, the police chief immediately sent the woman and child to the Caojiadu Branch. Director Wang immediately ordered Detective Team Leaders Wu Kezhong and Cao Chuqiao to go to 230 Baike Road with the police station detectives. They arrested Ling Kebing and his wife Ling Zhangshi (from Jiaxing), and also arrested Ling Desheng (renamed, 7 years old), a boy from Jiaxing who had just been abducted and was being sold, as well as a sales receipt and more than a dozen pawn tickets. They were all taken to the police station. They then sent police officers to the lime kiln to bring Li Li, the abductor, and Zhang Yunshou (29 years old, from Baoying), the father of the abducted child, to the police station. After separate interrogations by the police officers, the facts were confirmed. As the case involves the trafficking of children, which is a criminal offense, it was sentenced to be transferred to the General Bureau for interrogation after filing a report.

Impersonating Police Officers Extorting Money 174

Zong Jiao, a Cantonese doctor residing at 53 Dexing Lane, Peng Road, Hongkou, 32 years old, impersonated a public official of the French Police Department at 5 p.m. on the 4th of this month and went to the home of his fellow villager Su Pan at 1 Xiangxing Lane, 91 Dada Road, claiming to be investigating swallow nests and extorting 10 yuan, or else he would arrest her. Pan did not realize the truth and begged for mercy. Because she had no money, she only gave him 16 jiao. Zong took the money and hurriedly left in a rickshaw. He was spotted by his fellow villager Yuan Guiqiao, who followed Zong to the intersection of Aiduya Road and Jiangxi Road, where he shouted for the police and arrested Zong, who was taken to the British police station. The French police station sent detectives to take him back and send him to the Special Second Court for prosecution on charges of intimidation. As reported in the previous newspaper, the trial has concluded. Yesterday, Judge Cao sentenced Zong Jiao to eight months in prison and a fine of 500 yuan. The fine can be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be used to offset the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment.

Cao Zhenhai Sentenced for Arson 175

Cao Zhenhai, a 58-year-old man from Yangzhou, rented a cigarette and paper shop at 603 Ronghua Lane, Malang Road, French Concession, from Lin Rongbao, a Ningbo native, in February last year. The business was doing well. However, in February this year, Lin poached Cao's shop assistants, Wang Guanglan and Zhuang Ruixing, and jointly invested with Wang Guang, a native of Zhenjiang, to open a Ronghua store next to Cao's shop in Ronghua Lane, causing Cao's business and customers to be taken away. From then on, Cao's business failed and he suffered a loss. Cao harbored resentment. At midnight on the 9th of this month, he soaked cotton wool in kerosene and set fire to the shop, intending to burn down the Ronghua store and kill Lin's entire family to vent his anger. The fire was discovered by neighbors who alerted the fire department, which rushed to put out the fire. The police station investigated the cause of the fire and arrested Cao, who was sent to the Special Second Court for public prosecution. The trial proceedings were reported in the previous newspaper. After the interrogation was concluded, Judge Li Changnian of the Criminal Court sentenced Cao Zhenhai yesterday morning to eight months in prison for setting fire to his own residence and causing public danger. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be used to offset the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. After the sentencing, Cao was transferred to the detention center to await the appeal period before being sent to prison for execution.

Record of Opening Trial for Apprentice Death Case 176

At around 7 p.m. on September 4 of this year, Xie Arong and Ji Laosan formed a feud and fought in front of the Juxing Lane entrance of Xiangyan Bridge, Hongkou. As a result, someone fired a gun, and a stray bullet injured Liu Jinfa, a 21-year-old apprentice from Hangzhou who worked for Wuhua Ge Factory in Juxing Lane. He was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment but died. The local court sent personnel to verify and prepare the coffin. The police station arrested a suspect, Sun Jieshou, and sent him to the court. Prosecutor Li Fen interrogated him and determined that he was guilty of murder and filed a public prosecution. A court hearing was held some days ago. Sun vehemently denied the charges. The judge ordered the witnesses to be summoned for verification. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhang Shao specially opened the Fifth Court for trial. The defendant Sun Jieshou hired lawyer Zhang Ji to appear in court to defend him. The first witness, Zhu Dafu, testified that he was 21 years old, from Shanghai, and worked as a partner, manager, and general accountant for the Mingsheng Smelting Factory. Question: What position did Sun Jieshou hold in your factory? Answer: Supervisor. Our factory has a chief foreman Zhu Guifu and two supervisors, one is Sun Jieshou and the other is Chen Jinfen. Question: How many workers are there in total? Answer: Fifteen. Question: Did Sun Jieshou come to work at the factory on September 4? Answer: He came to the factory to work, arriving at the factory at 5:30 p.m. and starting the night shift at 6 o'clock. Question: Did you see Sun Jieshou? Answer: I saw him. The judge said, "This is a serious murder case, you can't say it casually." Answer: I really saw him. Question: What clothes did you see him wearing? Answer: He was wearing a black-gray Hua Te woolen long gown. Question: Did Sun Jieshou eat at the factory? Answer: Yes, he did. Question: How many people were at the same table? Answer: I, Sun Jieshou, Zhu Guihai, and six others were at the same table. The judge ordered Sun Jieshou to be brought to the case to testify. Question: What time did you enter the factory on September 4? Answer: I arrived at the factory at 5:30 p.m. and started work at 6 p.m. Question: What clothes did you wear that day? Answer: I wore a black Xiangyun gauze short gown and trousers. Question: Did you eat dinner? Answer: Yes, I did. Question: How many people ate at the same table? Answer: Eight people. The judge ordered Zhu Laosan to testify that the gun was held by Sun Jieshou. Because the swallow's nest opened by Xie Arong was captured by the police station, they said that I was "releasing the dragon," so they made things difficult for me. I was afraid of the gun, so I ran away and was not poisoned by the gun. At this point, Prosecutor Li came to the court and made a speech. The judge ordered the start of the debate. Lawyer Zhang Ji rose to defend the defendant for a long time. The judge ordered the debate to end and scheduled the sentencing for 10 a.m. on the 24th of this month. The defendant was returned to custody.

"Red Sheep Heroes" Receives Crowded Audiences 178

For the sake of promoting national spirit and commemorating revolutionary martyrs, the Gong Wu Stage has arranged to perform "Red Sheep Heroes." The three volumes have now been staged. The whole play takes Tang Zhengcai's training of the navy and Xiao Chaogui's death as two major backbones. Tang Zhengcai was the commander-in-chief of the navy when the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom sealed the navigation king. Tang Zhengcai's contribution was not small as the Taiping Army went down the river. The play describes Tang's respectable and tearful history in great detail. Zhao Xusheng, the new martial arts elder actor hired by the stage, played Tang Zhengcai and performed extremely hard. As for the role of King Xiao Chaogui of the West, Wang Huchen, the pillar of the stage, played the role, and the scene of being shot and killed in battle was more difficult and richer in national stimulation than Zhou Yu's "Woman Complain." Therefore, the seating has been quite crowded for several days.

City Sounds 184

Wanli Paint Factory Expanding News: The Wanli Paint Factory on Xietu Road in this city was established by Mr. Lei Dacheng, who gathered paint industry giants such as Mr. Feng Mingqing. Their "Sailboat" brand paints are popular throughout the country and the South Sea Islands. Later, due to various reasons, business could not be fully developed, failing to fully realize the initiators' original intention of saving the country through industry. Mr. Lei and Mr. Feng, aware of this, reorganized the company this autumn. The shareholders' meeting elected Ye Jisan, Zhang Hengfu, Fang Zhicheng, Wu Zeguang, Wu Xingqi, Wu Yinhuai, and Zhang Nanyuan as directors, and Hu Botao and Fang Wenbing as supervisors. Mr. Wu Yinhuai was appointed as manager. Since taking office, they have increased capital and actively reorganized. Regarding production, factory director Mr. Lei continues to research and improve, making the products even more refined than before. They also plan to send Mr. Lei to various cities across the country and the South Sea Islands for investigation.

Bent Company Opens Women's Fashion Department: Bent Brothers Company at 755 Jing'an Temple Road has established three departments: wool, Western clothing, and leather goods. All departments are thriving, especially the leather goods department, which has a wide variety of products, with a large stock of ready-made leather overcoats in all sizes. Recently, to meet the needs of women, a new women's fashion department has been established, employing Western female technicians to oversee the production of all kinds of women's clothing. The prices are especially fair.

Jicheng Pharmacy's Low-Price Gifts: The Jicheng Pharmacy at the Ballfield on Nanjing Road, due to the approaching year-end season, recognizes the need for timely nourishment for all those who work hard. Therefore, starting from the 20th of this month, the main store and branches will jointly hold a three-week large-scale low-price gift promotion. A variety of well-known tonics have been specially selected and offered at a special sacrifice, with one bottle given away for every bottle purchased. All other products under the "Ben" brand are discounted by 20%. Various biscuits and products from the Fus寿 Pharmaceutical Factory are also sold at a 20% discount. Foreign-brand products are also priced especially low. A variety of beautiful daily necessities are also prepared. For every purchase of "Ben" brand products totaling one yuan or foreign-brand products totaling two yuan, one item will be given away. The pharmacy's malt extract, cod liver oil, and other tonics have long been popular throughout the country. Now that they are all buy-one-get-one-free, it is expected that everyone will rush to buy them first.

Xu Kaixian and Wu Xuan Sacrifice Works: The Literary Supply Society at the intersection of Guizhou Road and Tianjin Road has been operating well since its establishment. Various gifts have been improved and are novel, such as various palladium coral flakes, cold gold paper, and brocade-mounted couplets, which are especially welcomed by society, and the prices are also very low. In order to reward customers, for every purchase of two yuan, a practical gift will be given. For every purchase of twenty yuan, either a ten-yuan carved bone from Mr. Wu Xuan or a silk couplet of calligraphy from Mr. Xu Kaixian will be given.

Painter Jia Ziyun's Remuneration Supports Disaster Relief: The painter Mr. Jia Ziyun came to Shanghai from Guangdong. Entertainment 187

Xiao Ling Seeks Her Mother, a Mingju Opera, to be Previewed at Shanghai University: The Mingju opera "Xiao Ling Seeks Her Mother" is the latest masterpiece by Ms. Liu Wang Liming. The play exposes the inhumanity of the maidservant system and serves as a warning to women who pursue free love. With songs, dances, the tears of a mother, and the innocence of children, it is the most interesting and touching social miniature. It is performed by the orphans of the Women and Children's Education Institute. This play was written by Ms. Wang for the Women's Temperance Association's charity entertainment event this autumn. It is reported that it will be publicly performed in Shanghai in mid-November. In order to improve further, the play is scheduled to be previewed tomorrow evening at the Shanghai University Auditorium in Yangshupu. Because it is a charitable event, tickets are priced slightly higher. In addition to the enthusiastic purchase of tickets by students and faculty families of the school, Ms. Wang's relatives and friends in Shanghai will also attend.

It is reported that the opening ceremony is scheduled for the evening of the 20th of this month, and there will surely be a grand occasion at that time.
